Khiyar al-Kashf When Seller Specifies Quantity After Contract
Explaining khiyar al-kashf when seller discloses quantity post-contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain khiyar al-kashf and apply it to scenarios where quantity is disclosed post-contract, identifying the buyer's option to accept or cancel the sale.

Core Idea
The buyer retains an option when actual quantity differs from his reasonable expectation, analogized to khiyar al-ru'yah.

In the sale of a heap of grain, the exact quantity may be unknown at contract time. When the seller later discloses the quantity, the buyer might find it differs from his expectation. This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling that the buyer then has an option (khiyar al-kashf) to accept the whole at a proportional price or cancel the sale, based on the analogy to khiyar al-ru'yah (option of inspection).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and legal issue
The passage considers a sale of a heap of grain where the quantity is unknown at contract. The seller later measures or states the quantity in the assembly. Determine the buyer's rights.
Focus on the buyer's expectation: e.g., he thought there would be 100 qafiz.
2
Trace the cause of the option
Understand that the option arises not from the seller's prior refusal to measure, but from the buyer's specific expectation that is now contradicted by the actual quantity.
The seller's later full disclosure does not remove the option; it triggers it.
3
Analyze the difficulties the buyer faces
If the heap is more than expected, the buyer lacks funds for the excess, cannot take it free, and taking only part forces a split on the seller. If less, he may need to buy elsewhere with uncertain quality.
These hardships justify giving the buyer an option.
4
Understand the analogy to khiyar al-ru'yah
The author equates this situation to khiyar al-ru'yah: just as a buyer who hasn't seen the item gets an option upon seeing it, here the buyer didn't know the quantity and gets an option upon learning it.
The analogy is based on shared illa: the buyer's reasonable expectation that may be disappointed.
5
Derive the Hanafi ruling
The buyer may either accept the entire heap at the rate per qafiz (total price divided by actual qafiz) or reject the whole sale. This is khiyar al-kashf.
The sale is valid (sahih) but the buyer has this option.

Source Text

کی جانب سے آیا ہے بایں طور کہ بائع تمام قفیزوں کی مقدار بیان کرنے یا مجلس میں کیل کرنے سے رک گیا ہے پس جب تفریق صفقة بائع کی جانب سے آیا تو بائع اس پر یقینا راضی ہوگا۔ اور جب بائع تفریق صفقة پر راضی ہے تو تفریق صفقة کی وجہ سے بائع کو اختیار دینے کے کیا معنی ہیں یعنی بائع کو کوئی اختیار نہ ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اس طرح اگر پورا ڈھیر مجلس کے اندر کیل کر لیا گیا یا بائع نے ڈھیر کے تمام قفیزوں کی مقدار بیان کر دی تو بھی مشتری کو اختیار ہوگا مگر یہ اختیار سابقہ علت کی وجہ سے نہیں ہوگا بلکہ اس وجہ سے ہوگا کہ مشتری کے خیال میں اس ڈھیر کی مقدار کا ایک اندازہ تھا مثلاً اس کا خیال تھا اس ڈھیر میں ایک سو قفیز ہوں گے اور اتنی ہی تقریباً اس کی ضرورت تھی اور اتنے ہی روپیوں کا نظم تھا۔ اب جب بعد میں اس ڈھیر کو ناپا یا بائع نے تمام قفیزوں کی مقدار بیان کی تو پتہ چلا کہ کل قفیز ایک سو سے زائد ہیں یا کم ہیں اگر زائد ہیں تو اس کی تین صورتیں ہیں ۔
(1) یہ کہ پورے کو پورے ثمن کے عوض لے لے۔
(۲) یا ایک سو قفیز کو ثمن کے عوض لے لے اور زائد کو مفت لے لے۔
اور یا زائد کو چھوڑ دے اور ایک سو کو لے لے۔
پہلی صورت تو اس لئے ممکن نہیں ہے کہ مشتری کے پاس ایک سو قفیز سے زائد کے لئے رقم نہیں ہے اور دوسری صورت یوں ممکن نہیں کہ بائع ایک سو قفیز سے زائد اناج مفت کیوں دے گا اور تیسری صورت اس لئے ممکن نہیں کہ اس میں بائع پر تفریق صفقة لازم آتا ہے اور اگر وہ ڈھیر ایک سو قفیز سے کم نکلا تو مشتری اپنی ضرورت کے مطابق ایک سو قفیز پورے کرنے کے لئے زائد اناج دوسری جگہ سے خریدے گا اب معلوم نہیں دوسری جگہ کا اناج اس کے موافق ہے یا نہیں ۔ بہر حال ان الجھنوں کی وجہ سے مشتری کو اختیار ہے کہ پورے ڈھیر کو کل قفیز بدرہم کے حساب سے لے لے یا پورے کو چھوڑ دے اس خیار کا نام خیار کشف ہے۔ کیونکہ کل مقدار جو عقد بیع کے وقت معلوم نہیں تھی وہ اب بائع کے بیان کر دینے یا کیل کر دینے سے معلوم ہوئی ہے اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے مشتری نے عقد بیع کے وقت مبیع کو نہیں دیکھا تھا بعد میں دیکھا تو مشتری کو لینے یا نہ لینے کا خیار حاصل ہے اسی طرح مسئلہ مذکورہ میں بھی مشتری کو لینے یا نہ لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔
It comes from the side that the seller refrained from stating the quantity of all qafizes or measuring in the assembly. So when the separation of the contract comes from the seller's side, the seller will definitely be pleased with it. And when the seller is pleased with the separation of the contract, what meaning is there in giving the seller an option due to separation of the contract? That is, the seller will have no option. The author of Hidayah says: In this manner, if the entire heap was measured within the assembly or the seller stated the quantity of all the qafizes of the heap, even then the buyer will have an option, but this option will not be due to the previous cause, rather it will be because the buyer had an estimation of the quantity of this heap in his mind, for example, he thought this heap would have a hundred qafizes, and approximately that was his need, and he had arranged that many rupees. Now, when later he measured the heap or the seller stated the quantity of all the qafizes, it became known that the total qafizes are more or less than a hundred. If they are more, there are three possibilities: (1) He takes the whole for the whole price. (2) Or he takes a hundred qafizes for the price and takes the excess for free. (3) Or he leaves the excess and takes a hundred. The first possibility is not possible because the buyer does not have money for more than a hundred qafizes. The second possibility is not possible because why would the seller give the excess grain for free. The third possibility is not possible because it necessitates division of the contract for the seller. And if the heap is found to be less than a hundred qafizes, the buyer will buy additional grain from another place to complete a hundred qafizes, but it is not known whether the grain from the other place matches this one or not. In any case, due to these difficulties, the buyer has the option to take the entire heap at the rate of each qafiz for a dirham or to leave the whole. This option is called khiyar al-kashf (option of disclosure). Because the total quantity, which was not known at the time of the contract, has now become known due to the seller's statement or measurement. And this is like the buyer did not see the sold item at the time of the contract; when he saw it later, he has the option to take it or not. Similarly, in the mentioned case, the buyer will have the option to take or not.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage explains khiyar al-kashf (option of disclosure) in the context of selling a heap of grain when the total quantity is unknown at the time of contract but later becomes known through the seller's disclosure or measurement. The passage begins by discussing a prior scenario where the seller refrained from measuring or stating the quantity, and then the separation of the contract came from the seller. In that case, the seller has no option because he caused the separation. The main ruling, from the author of al-Hidayah, is that even if the seller measures the entire heap in the assembly or states the quantity, the buyer still retains an option. However, the basis for this option is not the same as in the previous case (where the seller had refrained). Instead, it is because the buyer had a specific expectation about the quantity (e.g., one hundred qafizes) based on his need and financial planning. After the actual quantity becomes known, if there is a discrepancy, the buyer faces practical difficulties: he cannot take the excess without additional funds, the seller will not give it for free, and taking only a portion forces division of the contract on the seller. If it is less, the buyer may need to purchase elsewhere, but the quality may differ. Therefore, to avoid hardship, the buyer is given the option to either accept the entire heap at the proportional price per qafiz (calculated based on the total price divided by the number of qafizes) or to reject the entire sale. This option is equated to khiyar al-ru'yah (option of inspection), where the buyer has the right to rescind upon seeing the item unseen at contract. The ruling is consistent with the Hanafi principle of avoiding gharar (uncertainty) that leads to disputes. The authority weight is from the commentary on al-Hidayah, which is based on the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
خیار کشف (khiyar al-kashf): The option of disclosure: the buyer's right to ratify or cancel a sale when the quantity or quality of the sold item becomes known after the contract.
تفریق صفقة (tafriq al-safqah): The separation or division of the contract, i.e., rescinding part of the sale.
قفیز (qafiz): A unit of volume measurement for grain, varying by region.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the sale of a heap of grain with an unknown total quantity, after the seller measures the entire heap in the assembly, the buyer:
A) Must accept the heap at the agreed price per qafiz.
B) Has no option because the seller has fulfilled his duty.
C) Has the option (khiyar) to take the entire heap at the proportional rate or to cancel the sale.
D) May only take a portion equal to his estimate.

Key Takeaway
When a sale's quantity is unknown at contract and later disclosed, the Hanafi school grants the buyer khiyar al-kashf to avoid hardship.

Selling Flock Per Sheep and Cloth Per Cubit: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Unspecified Quantities
Intra-Hanafi dispute on selling per unit without specifying total

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on selling a flock of sheep with a per-unit price without specifying total quantity, and apply the distinction between uniform and varied items to determine the validity of such sales.

Core Idea
Uncertainty that provokes dispute invalidates a sale; removable ignorance does not, but variation among items makes removal impossible.

This passage addresses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: can you sell a flock of sheep or a piece of cloth by stating a per-unit price without specifying the total quantity? Imam Abu Hanifa holds the entire sale invalid due to excessive uncertainty, while the two Sahibayn deem it valid because the parties can resolve the uncertainty themselves. The critical factor is whether the items are uniform or varied, as this determines if ignorance leads to dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Contract and the Problem
Recognise that the contract specifies a unit price (e.g., each sheep for a dirham) but does not state the total number of units or the total price. This creates uncertainty (jahala) about the overall subject matter and price.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position and His Evidence
Abu Hanifa rules that the entire transaction is invalid (fasid). His evidence: both the total quantity and total price are unknown, making the contract impossibly uncertain. Even if limited to one unit, the sale of a single sheep or cubit is also invalid because the specific unit is unidentified and the individuals vary in value, leading to inevitable dispute (niza').
3
State the Sahibayn's Position and Their Evidence
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule that the sale of the entire lot is valid (ja'iz). Their evidence: the ignorance is removable—the parties can count or measure the items. Removable ignorance does not invalidate a contract. They accept that the sale reverts to one unit if not specified, but they uphold the validity of the whole.
4
Analyse the Distinction: Varied vs. Uniform Items
Abu Hanifa distinguishes between items whose individuals vary in value (e.g., sheep, handwoven cloth) and uniform items (e.g., grain in a heap). For uniform items, selling an unspecified unit (e.g., one qafiz from a heap) is valid because all parts are identical, so uncertainty does not lead to dispute. For varied items, any unspecified unit is problematic.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
The ruling affects everyday transactions: according to Abu Hanifa, such sales are invalid and must be restructured (e.g., specify total). According to the Sahibayn, they are valid as long as the parties can later determine the specifics. The mufta bihi (operative opinion) in later fatwa is usually the Sahibayn's view for ease of transactions, though caution is recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بكریوں کے گلے میں ایک بکری کی ایک درہم کے بدلے بیع کا حکم
ومن باع قطيع غنم كل شاة بدرهم فسد البيع في جميعها عند ابي حنيفة و كذالك من باع ثوبا مدارة كل ذراع بدرهم ولم يسم جملة الذرعان وكذا كل معدود متفاوت وعندهما يجوز في الكل لما قلنا وعنده ينصرف الى الواحد لما بينا غير أن بيع شاة من قطيع و ذراع من ثوب لا يجوز للتفاوت وبيع قفيز من صبرة يجوز لعدم التفاوت فلا تفضي الجهالة الى المنازعة فيه وتفضي اليها في الأول فوضح الفرق
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے بکریوں کا ایک گلہ بعوض ایک درہم ایک بکری کے حساب سے فروخت کیا تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک تمام بکریوں کی بیع فاسد ہے اور اسی طرح اگر گزوں کی ناپ سے کوئی کپڑا بحساب ایک درہم فی گز کے فروخت کیا اور تمام گز بیان نہیں کئے اور یہی حکم ہر معدود متفاوت چیز کا ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک تمام کی بیع جائز ہے۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی۔ اور ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک یہ بیع صرف ایک کی طرف راجع ہوگی۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی۔ مگر یہ کہ گلہ میں سے ایک بکری اور تھان میں سے ایک گز کی بیع بھی تفاوت کی وجہ سے جائز نہیں ہے اور ڈھیر میں سے ایک قفیز کی بیع تفاوت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے جائز ہے۔ پس چونکہ ڈھیر میں سے ایک قفیز کی بیع میں جہالت مفضی الی المنازعہ نہیں ہے اور گلہ میں سے ایک بکری اور تھان میں سے ایک گز کی بیع میں جہالت صریح مفضی الی المنازعہ ہے۔ اس لئے فرق ظاہر ہو گیا۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے بکریوں کا گلہ (ریوڑ) یہ کہہ کر فروخت کیا کہ ہر بکری ایک درہم کے عوض ہے تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک تمام بکریوں میں بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی یا کپڑے کا ایک تھان یہ کہہ کر فروخت کیا کہ ہر گز ایک درہم کے عوض ہے اور تمام گزوں کی تعداد اور تمام گزوں کا ثمن بیان نہیں کیا تو اس صورت میں بھی تمام گزوں میں بیع فاسد ہوگی۔ اور اسی طرح ہر ایسی چیز کہ جس کو شمار کر کے بیچا جاتا ہے اور اس کے افراد میں قیمت کے اعتبار سے تفاوت ہوتا ہے تو ان کی بیع بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ جیسے تربوز کدو لوکی۔ صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ بکریوں کے پورے گلہ اور پورے تھان کی بیع جائز ہے اور دلیل سابق میں گزر چکی کہ مبیع اور ثمن اگر چہ مجہول ہیں لیکن ان کی جہالت کا دور کرنا خود ان کے ہاتھ میں ہے۔ بایں طور کہ گلہ کی بکریوں کو شمار کر لیں اور تھان کو ناپ لیں یا بائع ان کی مقدار کو بیان کردے۔ اور ایسی جہالت کا دور کرنا عاقدین کے ہاتھ میں ہو، جو از بیع کے لئے مانع نہیں ہوتی ہے اس لئے یہاں پورے گلہ اور پورے تھان کی بیع جائز ہوگی۔
حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مبیع (یعنی تمام بکریوں کی مقدار اور تھان کے تمام گزوں کی مقدار) اور ثمن کے مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے تمام بکریوں اور تمام گزوں کی بیع کو جائز قرار دینا متعذر اور ناممکن ہے اس لئے اقل یعنی ایک کی طرف بیع کو پھیرا جائے گا۔ پس گلہ میں سے ایک بکری کی بیع اور تھان میں سے ایک گز کی بیع درست ہونی چاہیے مگر چونکہ گلہ کی بکریوں میں قیمت کے اعتبار سے بہت بڑا فرق ہوتا ہے کسی بکری کی قیمت زیادہ ہوتی ہے کسی کی کم ہوتی ہے۔ اس طرح تھان کے گزوں میں تفاوت ہوتا ہے لیکن یہ تفاوت اس تھان کے گزوں میں ہوتا ہے جو ہاتھ سے بنا جاتا ہے آج کل کے تھان جوٹل میں بنے جاتے ہیں ان کے افراد میں تفاوت نہیں ہوتا بہر حال بکریوں اور تھان کے افراد میں تفاوت کی وجہ سے ایک بکری اور ایک گز کے اندر بھی بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اور اناج کے ڈھیر کے قفیزوں میں چونکہ کوئی تفاوت نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے ڈھیر میں سے ایک قفیز کی بیع جائز ہوگی۔
حاصل یہ کہ بکریوں اور تھان کے افراد میں چونکہ قیمت کے اعتبار سے تفاوت ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے گلہ میں سے ایک بکری اور تھان میں سے ایک گز جس کو مبیع قرار دیا جائے گا وہ مجہول ہے اور مجہول بھی ایسا جو جھگڑا پیدا کرے گا، بایں طور کہ بائع کم قیمت کی بکری اور تھان میں سے ایک گز دے گا اور مشتری کی پوری کوشش یہ ہوگی کہ قیمتی سے قیمتی بکری اور تھان میں سے گز لے اور ڈھیر کے تمام قفیز چونکہ قیمت کے اعتبار سے مساوی اور برابر ہوتے ہیں اس لئے ڈھیر میں سے ایک قفیز اگر چہ مجہول ہے مگر ایسا مجہول نہیں جو مفضی الی المنازعہ ہو پس اس فرق کی بنیاد پر حضرت امام الہمام قدوۃ الا نام عالی مقام مقتداہ جنت المقام ابو حنیفہ نور اللہ مرقدہ نے ڈھیر میں سے ایک قفیز کی بیع کو جائز قرار دیا اور گلہ میں سے ایک بکری اور تھان میں سے ایک گز کی بیع کو ناجائز قرار دیا۔
Ruling on selling a flock of sheep with each sheep for a dirham.
And whoever sold a flock of sheep, each sheep for a dirham, the sale is invalid in all of them according to Abu Hanifa. Similarly, whoever sold a cloth measured by the cubit, each cubit for a dirham, and did not specify the total cubits, and similarly every enumerated item with variation. And according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is permissible in all, due to what we said. And according to him (Abu Hanifa), it refers to one, due to what we explained. However, the sale of one sheep from the flock and one cubit from the cloth is not permissible due to variation. And the sale of one qafiz from a heap is permissible due to lack of variation. So ignorance (jahala) does not lead to dispute in it, but leads to dispute in the first, so the difference is clear.
Translation: And the person who sold a flock of sheep in exchange for one dirham per sheep, then according to Abu Hanifa the sale of all sheep is invalid. Similarly, if a cloth was sold by cubit measurement, per dirham per cubit, and all cubits were not stated, this ruling applies to every enumerated item with variation. According to the two (Sahibayn), the sale of all is permissible, due to the evidence we mentioned. According to Abu Hanifa, this sale will revert to only one, due to the evidence we mentioned. But the sale of one sheep from the flock and one cubit from the cloth is also not permissible due to variation, and the sale of one qafiz from a heap is permissible due to lack of variation. Since in the sale of one qafiz from a heap, the ignorance does not lead to dispute, and in the sale of one sheep from the flock and one cubit from the cloth, the ignorance is clear and leads to dispute, therefore the difference is clear.
Explanation of the issue: If someone sold a flock of sheep saying 'each sheep for a dirham', then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the sale of all sheep will be invalid; or if he sold a cloth saying 'each cubit for a dirham' and did not state the number of all cubits and the total price of all cubits, then in that case also the sale of all cubits is invalid. Similarly, every item that is sold by count and whose individuals differ in value, their sale is also not permissible, such as watermelon, pumpkin, bottle gourd. The two (Sahibayn) have said that the sale of the entire flock and the entire cloth is permissible, and the evidence has passed previously that even though the sold item and the price are unknown, the removal of that ignorance is in their own hands, i.e., they can count the sheep of the flock and measure the cloth, or the seller can state its quantity. And such ignorance that can be removed by the contracting parties does not prevent the validity of the sale, therefore here the sale of the entire flock and the entire cloth is permissible.
The evidence of Imam Abu Hanifa is that because the sold item (i.e., the quantity of all sheep and the quantity of all cubits of the cloth) and the price are unknown, it is impossible and not feasible to validate the sale of all sheep and all cubits, so the sale will be turned towards the minimum, i.e., one. Therefore, the sale of one sheep from the flock and one cubit from the cloth should be valid, but because there is a great difference in value among the sheep of the flock (some sheep are high-priced, some low), similarly there is variation among the cubits of the cloth, but this variation exists in cloth that is handwoven; nowadays cloth is manufactured in [؟] and its individuals have no variation. In any case, due to variation among the individuals of sheep and cloth, the sale of one sheep and one cubit is also not permissible. And because there is no variation among the qafizes of a grain heap, therefore the sale of one qafiz from the heap is permissible.
Conclusion: Since there is variation in value among the individuals of sheep and cloth, therefore when one sheep from the flock and one cubit from the cloth is made the sold item, it is unknown, and such an unknown that will cause dispute: the seller will give a low-value sheep and a low-quality cubit, and the buyer will strive to get the most valuable sheep and the best cubit. Since all qafizes of the heap are equal and identical in value, therefore one qafiz from the heap, although unknown, is not such an unknown that leads to dispute. Based on this difference, Imam Abu Hanifa declared the sale of one qafiz from the heap permissible, and declared the sale of one sheep from the flock and one cubit from the cloth impermissible.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of selling a flock of sheep or a piece of cloth with a unit price but without specifying the total quantity. The case involves selling a flock of sheep 'each sheep for a dirham' without stating the total number, and similarly selling a cloth 'each cubit for a dirham' without stating the total cubits. The ruling also applies to any counted item whose individuals vary in value (e.g., watermelons, pumpkins). Abu Hanifa rules that the sale of the entire flock or cloth is invalid (fasid) due to ignorance (jahala) of both the total sold item and the total price, which leads to excessive uncertainty. The sale is then redirected to a single unit (the least possible), but even the sale of a single unit is invalid due to variation among individuals, as the specific sheep or cubit is unidentified and likely to cause dispute (niza'). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the sale is valid for the entire flock or cloth. Their reasoning is that the individuals are capable of being counted or measured, and the contracting parties can remove the ignorance themselves; such removable ignorance does not negate the contract. The passage then clarifies the distinction between items with variation (like sheep and handwoven cloth) and uniform items (like grain in a heap). For uniform items, the sale of a single undefined unit (e.g., one qafiz from a heap) is valid because all parts are identical, so there is no cause for dispute. The commentary elaborates on the arguments, noting that modern machine-made cloth may lack variation, but the ruling is based on traditional handwoven cloth. The final conclusion reiterates Abu Hanifa's position: the sale of one qafiz from a heap is valid due to uniformity, but the sale of one sheep from a flock or one cubit from a cloth is invalid due to variation leading to dispute. The authority weight of this dispute is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, as it is a well-known ikhtilaf recorded in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
معدود متفاوت (ma'dud mutafawit): Countable items whose individual units differ in value, such as sheep in a flock or cubits of handwoven cloth.
تفاوت (tafawut): Variation or difference in value among the individual units of a sold item.
جہالت (jahala): Ignorance or uncertainty about the essential specifications of the sold item or price.
مفضی الی المنازعہ (mufdi ila al-munaza'ah): Leading to dispute; a degree of uncertainty that is likely to cause conflict between the parties.
صبرہ (subrah): A heap of grain or similar uniform commodity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is selling one qafiz from a grain heap valid while selling one sheep from a flock is not?
A) Sheep are alive.
B) Grain qafizes are uniform; sheep vary.
C) Grain is food.
D) Sheep require a separate contract.

Key Takeaway
Uncertainty that can be removed without causing dispute does not invalidate a sale, but uncertainty over varied items that inevitably leads to conflict renders the sale invalid.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Dispute on Selling a Flock or Bolt with Unspecified Quantity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on jahalah in sales

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-madhhab dispute on selling items with quantity uncertainty and distinguish between removable and unremovable ignorance (jahalah) based on price variance (tafawut).

Core Idea
Jahalah that can be removed does not invalidate; price variance among units creates irremovable dispute.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the sale of a flock of goats or a bolt of cloth when the price is per unit but total quantity is not specified. The key is whether the ignorance (jahalah) about the total is removable by the parties or leads to unavoidable dispute. We will trace both proofs and see how the concept of price variance (tafawut) shapes the ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the issue: sale of entire flock/bolt with per-unit price but unknown total. Within the Hanafi school, two opinions exist: Sahibayn say valid, Abu Hanifa says fasid.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the sale of the entire flock or bolt is valid. Their proof: the jahalah (ignorance of total quantity and price) can be easily removed by counting or measuring.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Sahibayn argue that because the jahalah is removable by the parties themselves, it does not lead to dispute and thus does not invalidate the contract.
The key distinction: jahalah that can be easily removed is not fatal.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa's proof: the total sold item and total price are both unknown, so the contract cannot be valid for the entire amount. It defaults to one unit, but even one unit is unknown due to price variance among goats or yards, leading to inevitable dispute.
Contrast with grain heap: no variance, so one qafiz is valid.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Under Sahibayn, the sale of the entire flock at a per-goat price is valid; under Abu Hanifa, it is not. The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view.
Important for fatwa: follow the Sahibayn.

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے بکریوں کا گلہ ( ریوڑ) یہ کہ کر فروخت کیا کہ ہر بکری ایک درہم کے عوض ہے تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک تمام بکریوں میں بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی یا کپڑے کا ایک تھان یہ کہ کر فروخت کیا کہ ہرگز ایک درہم کے عوض ہے اور تمام گروں کی تعداد اور تمام گزوں کا شمن بیان نہیں کیا تو اس صورت میں بھی تمام گڑوں میں بیچ فاسد ہوگی ۔ اور اسی طرح ہر ایسی چیز کہ جس کو شمار کر کے بیچا جاتا ہے اور اس کے افراد میں قیمت کے اعتبار سے تفاوت ہوتا ہے تو ان کی بیع بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ جیسے تربوز کدو لوکی ۔ صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ بکریوں کے پورے گلہ اور پورے تھان کی بیع جائز ہے اور دلیل سابق میں گزر چکی کہ مبیع اور شمن اگر چہ مجہول ہیں لیکن ان کی جہالت کا دور کرنا خود ان کے ہاتھ میں ہے۔ بایں طور کہ گلہ کی بکریوں کو شمار کر لیں اور تھان کو ناپ لیں یا بائع ان کی مقدار کو بیان کردے۔ اور ایسی جہالت کا دور کرنا عاقدین کے ہاتھ میں ہو، جو از بیچ کے لئے مانع نہیں ہوتی ہے اس لئے یہاں پورے گلہ اور پورے تھان کی بیج جائز ہوگی۔
حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مبیع ( یعنی تمام بکریوں کی مقدار اور تھان کے تمام گزوں کی مقدار ) اور شمن کے مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے تمام بکریوں اور تمام گزوں کی بیع کو جائز قرار دینا تو متعد راور ناممکن ہے اس لئے اقل یعنی ایک کی طرف بیع کو پھیرا جائے گا۔ پس گلہ میں سے ایک بکری کی بیچ اور تھان میں سے ایک گز کی بیع درست ہونی چاہیے مگر چونکہ گلہ کی بکریوں میں قیمت کے اعتبار سے بہت بڑا فرق ہوتا ہے کسی بکری کی قیمت زیادہ ہوتی لیے کسی کی کم ہوتی ہے۔ اس طرح تھان کے گڑوں میں تفاوت ہوتا ہے لیکن یہ تفاوت اس تھان کے گڑوں میں ہوتا ہے جو ہاتھ سے بنا جاتا ہے آج کل کے تھان جوٹل میں منے جاتے ہیں ان کے اطراف میں تفاوت نہیں ہوتا بہر حال بکریوں اور تھان کے اطراف میں تفاوت کی وجہ سے ایک بکری اور ایک گز کے اندر بھی بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اور اناج کے ڈھیر کے قفیزوں میں چونکہ کوئی تفاوت نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لے ڈھیر میں سے ایک قفیز کی بیع جائز ہوگی۔

Page 38: Book of Sales. Ashraf al-Bidayah Sharh Urdu Hidayah Volume 8. [This applies to] every counted item that varies [in value]. According to the Sahibayn, the sale of the entire [flock/bolt] is valid, due to the proof we have mentioned. According to Abu Hanifa, the sale reverts to only one, due to the proof we have mentioned. However, the sale of one goat from the flock and one yard from the bolt is also invalid due to variance, while the sale of one qafiz from a heap is valid due to lack of variance. Since in the sale of one qafiz from a heap there is no ignorance leading to dispute, whereas in the sale of one goat from a flock and one yard from a bolt the ignorance is apparent and leads to dispute, therefore the difference becomes clear. Explanation of the issue: If someone sold a flock of goats saying 'each goat for one dirham', then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the entire sale is invalid. Similarly, if he sold a bolt of cloth saying 'each yard for one dirham' without specifying the total number of yards and the price of all yards, then the sale of all yards is also invalid. Likewise, every item that is sold by count and whose individual units vary in price—such as watermelons, pumpkins, and bottle gourds—its sale is not valid. The Sahibayn have stated that the sale of the entire flock and the entire bolt is valid, and the proof has already passed: even though the sold item and the price are unknown, removing that ignorance is in their hands—by counting the goats in the flock, measuring the bolt, or the seller stating the quantities. Such ignorance that can be removed by the contracting parties does not prevent the sale, therefore the sale of the entire flock and entire bolt is valid here. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that due to the sold item (the quantity of all goats and yards) and the price being unknown, validating the sale of all goats and all yards is impossible, so the sale is turned towards the minimum, i.e., one. Thus the sale of one goat from the flock and one yard from the bolt should be valid. However, since goats in a flock vary greatly in price—some more expensive, some cheaper—and similarly yards in a handwoven bolt vary—though today's machine-made bolts have no variance in their yards—nevertheless, due to variance among goats and yards, the sale of one goat and one yard is also not valid. As for qafizes in a heap of grain, since there is no variance, the sale of one qafiz from the heap is valid. The conclusion: since goats and yards vary in price, one goat from the flock and one yard from the bolt, if made the sold item, are unknown and such ignorance that will lead to dispute—the seller will give a low-value goat/yard and the buyer will try to get the highest-value one. But all qafizes in a heap are equal in price, so one qafiz, though unknown, is not such ignorance that leads to dispute. On this basis, Imam Abu Hanifa, may Allah illuminate his grave, declared the sale of one qafiz from a heap valid, and the sale of one goat from a flock and one yard from a bolt invalid.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the sale of a flock of goats or a bolt of cloth when the price is per unit but the total quantity is unspecified. The key issue is ignorance (jahalah) that leads to dispute (munaza'ah). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the sale of the entire flock/bolt is valid because the ignorance can be removed by counting or measuring; such removable ignorance does not invalidate the contract. Abu Hanifa argues that since both the total quantity and total price are unknown, the contract cannot be valid for the whole; it defaults to a single unit. However, even the sale of one unit from a flock/bolt is invalid due to price variance among individuals—this creates a jahalah that leads to dispute. In contrast, grain from a heap is uniform, so selling one qafiz is valid despite the quantity being undetermined. The text explains that variance among individuals (tafawut) is the critical factor. The commentary clarifies that the ruling applies to all counted items with price variance, like fruits. The author concludes that Abu Hanifa's position is consistent: no sale where jahalah leads to dispute.

Key Terms
جہالت (jahalah): Ignorance about essential aspects of the contract, such as quantity or price, that can lead to dispute.
تفاوت (tafawut): Variance in value among individual units of a species, e.g., different prices for different goats in a flock.
صفقہ (safqah): The contract of sale; here used in the context of the bargain being concluded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the sale of one goat from a flock invalid?
A) Because the goat is not specified
B) Because goats vary in price, leading to dispute
C) Because the price is unknown
D) Because the flock size is unknown

Key Takeaway
The operative Hanafi position is that a sale with unstated total quantity is valid if the ignorance can be removed, unless the items vary significantly in value leading to inevitable dispute.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Ruling on Buying a Heap of Grain: Shortfall and Excess
Ruling on buyer's option and seller's right in a grain heap sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a heap of grain is found to be less or more than the specified quantity, and identify the option available to the buyer.

Core Idea
If the heap is short, buyer has option; if excess, extra belongs to seller.

This lesson presents a clear ruling from al-Quduri on a common sales scenario: buying a heap of grain with a stated quantity. The ruling distinguishes between a shortfall and an excess, each with a different consequence. Understanding this ruling requires recognizing that quantity is considered the essence of the sale, not a mere description.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage gives two outcomes: if the heap is less than specified, and if it is more. First, note each scenario separately.
2
Analyze the shortfall scenario
The buyer has a choice: take the existing amount at a proportionate price or cancel the sale. The reason is that the contract was broken before completion—the buyer's consent was for the full quantity, not the lesser.
The option is khiyar al-tafarrud (option due to partition of the bargain).
3
Analyze the excess scenario
The excess belongs to the seller because the sale was for a specific quantity. Since quantity is the essence (asl), the contract cannot include more than what was agreed.
The buyer does not get a proportional price increase.
4
Understand the rationale
The ruling hinges on the distinction between essence and description. For measured and weighed items, quantity is essence; for counted items, quantity is a description.
This distinction affects whether a change in quantity adjusts the price.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غلہ کی ایک ڈھیری اس شرط پر خریدی کہ سو فیز سو درہم کے بدلے کم یا زیادہ ہوں تو بیع کا حکم
قال ومن ابتاع صبرة طعام على انهامائة قفيز بمائة درهم فوجدها اقل كان المشترى بالخيار ان شاء اخذ الموجود بحصته من الثمن و ان شاء فسخ البيع لتفرق الصفقة عليه قبل التمام فلم يتم رضاه بالموجود ان وجدها اكثر فالزيادة للبائع لان البيع وقع على مقدار معين و القدر ليس بوصف
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا اور جس شخص نے اناج کی ایک ڈھیری اس شرط پر خریدی سوقفی سو درہم کے عوض ہیں ۔ پھر مشترکی نے اس کو کم پایا تو مشتری کو اختیار ہوگا کہ اگر چاہے مقدار موجودہ کو اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض لے لے اور اگر چاہے تو بیع فسخ کر دے کیونکہ عقد تمام ہونے سے پہلے اس پر صفقہ متفرق ہو گیا تو مقدار موجود کے ساتھ اس کی رضا مندی پوری نہ ہوئی اور اگر مشتری نے ڈھیری کو سو قفیز سے زیادہ پایا تو زیادتی بائع کی ہوگی۔ کیونکہ بیچ ایک مقدار معین پر واقع ہوئی ہے اور مقدار وصف نہیں ہے۔
تشریح قدر (اصل) اور وصف کے درمیان فرق یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی چیز ٹکڑے کرنے سے عیب دار ہو جاتی ہے تو کمی اور زیادتی اس میں وصف ہوتی ہے۔ اور اگر ٹکڑے کرنے سے عیب دار نہ ہوتی ہو تو زیادہ اور نقصان اس میں اصل ہے پس قلت اور کثرت مکسیلات اور موزونات میں اصل ہے اور ذراع نذروعات میں وصف ہے۔ دوسری بات یہ ذہن میں رکھئے کہ اصل یعنی قدر کے مقابلے میں شمن آتا ہے یعنی اصل مئی کے کم اور زیادہ ہونے سے ثمن کم اور زیادہ نہیں ہوتا ۔
رت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے اناج کی ایک ڈھیری اس شرط پر خریدی کہ یہ سو فیز میں سو درہم کے عوض گویا سو فیز وں کا معاملہ سو درہم کے عوض کیا۔ پھر ناپ کر پتہ چلا کہ سو قفیز سے کم ہیں مثلا نوے فیز ہیں تو مشتری کو اختیار ہوگا کہ مقدار موجود یعنی نوسے قفیر کو اسکے کم تو حصہ ثمن یعنی نوے درہم کے عوض لے لے اور چاہے تو بیع کو فتح کر دے۔ اس اختیار کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد تمام ہونے سے پہلے مشتری پر صفقہ متفرق ہو گیا ہے اس طور پر کہ معاملہ ہوا تھا سو فیزوں کا اور یہاں موجود ہیں نوے قفیز اور یہی صفقہ کا بدلنا ہے اور چونکہ مشتری نے مبیع پر قبضہ نہیں کیا اور اس کی رضامندی مکمل نہیں ہوئی۔ اس لئے عقد بھی تمام نہیں ہوا تو گویا تمام عقد سے پہلے صفقہ متفرق ہو گیا ۔ اور جب صفقہ متفرق ہو گیا تو مقدار موجودہ پر مشتری کی رضامندی مکمل نہ ہوگی۔ اور جب مشتری کی رضامندی مکمل نہیں ہوئی تو اس کو لینے اور نہ لینے کا اختیار ہوگا۔
اور اگر مشتری نے اس ڈھیر کو سو فیز سے زیادہ پایا تو زیادتی بائع کے لئے ہوگی کیونکہ مبیع مقدار معین پر واقع ہوئی ہے اور جو چیز مقدار معین پر واقع ہو وہ اس کے علاوہ کو شامل نہیں ہوتی الا یہ کہ وہ زائد از قبیلہ وصف ہو۔ اور مقدار معین پر جوزائد مقدار ہے وہ وصف نہیں ہے بلکہ اصل اور از قبیلہ مقدار ہے۔ اس لئے بیع اس زائد مقدار کو شامل نہ ہوگی اور جب بیع مقدار زائد کو شامل نہ ہوئی تو زیادتی بائع کے لئے ہوگی نہ کہ مشتری کے لئے۔ کیوں کہ مشتری کے لئے وہی چیز ہوتی ہے جس کو عقد بیع شامل ہوتا ہے۔
Ruling on buying a heap of grain on condition that it is one hundred qafizes for one hundred dirhams, whether less or more. He (al-Quduri) said: And whoever bought a heap of grain on condition that it is one hundred qafizes for one hundred dirhams, and then found it less, the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he may take what is present in proportion to its share of the price, and if he wishes, he may rescind the sale because the contract was broken before completion, so his consent to the present quantity was not perfected. And if he found it more, the excess belongs to the seller, because the sale was contracted on a specific quantity, and quantity is not a description. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And whoever bought a heap of grain on condition that it is one hundred qafizes for one hundred dirhams, then the buyer found it less, he has the option: if he wishes, he may take the present quantity in exchange for its share of the price (i.e., ninety dirhams), and if he wishes, he may cancel the sale. The reason for this option is that the contract broke apart for him before completion; since the contract was for a hundred qafizes and only ninety are present, the bargain is different. And because the buyer did not take possession and his consent was not complete, the contract was not completed; so it is as if the bargain broke before completion. When the bargain breaks, the buyer's consent to the existing quantity is not complete, so he has the choice to take or not. And if the buyer found the heap more than a hundred qafizes, the excess belongs to the seller because the sale was contracted on a specific quantity, and what is contracted on a specific quantity does not include anything beyond it unless the excess is of the category of description. And the excess in quantity is not a description; it is rather from the category of quantity itself. Therefore the sale does not include the excess quantity. When the sale does not include the excess, the excess belongs to the seller, not the buyer, because the buyer only takes what the contract includes.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from al-Quduri on a specific sale scenario: buying a grain heap with the condition that it contains a specified number of qafizes (a volume measure). The ruling has two parts: (1) if the heap is less than specified, the buyer has an option (khiyar) to either accept the existing quantity at a proportionate price or cancel the sale; (2) if it is more, the excess belongs to the seller. The commentary explains the reasoning: the contract was based on a specific quantity, and quantity is considered the essence (asl), not a mere description (wasf). Therefore, any increase or decrease in quantity does not adjust the price automatically. For shortfall, the contract is considered broken before completion because the subject matter differs; the buyer's consent was not for the lesser amount. For excess, the contract only covers the agreed amount, so extra remains seller's property. The commentary also clarifies the distinction between 'asl (essence/quantity) and wasf (description): if an item becomes defective when divided, its quantity is a description; otherwise it is the essence. For measured and weighed items, quantity is the essence; for counted items like lengths, quantity is a description. This affects rulings on sales.

Key Terms
صبرہ (sibrah): A heap or pile of grain, sold as a bulk without exact measurement but with a specified supposed quantity.
قفیز (qafiz): A unit of dry measure for grain, varying by region but standardized in fiqh texts.
اصل (asl): The essence or substance of a thing; here contrasted with wasf (description). Quantity is asl for measured/weighed items, not a wasf.
وصف (wasf): A description or quality of an item; in this context, if quantity were a description, a change would adjust price, but it is ruled as asl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a buyer purchases a heap of grain on condition of 100 qafiz for 100 dirhams, and finds it to be 110 qafiz, what is the ruling?
A) The buyer must pay 110 dirhams and take all
B) The buyer can cancel the sale
C) The extra 10 qafiz belong to the seller without additional payment
D) The extra 10 qafiz belong to the buyer

Key Takeaway
In a sale of a specific quantity of grain, the buyer has an option on shortfall, but any excess automatically belongs to the seller.

Sale of Grain with Stipulated Quantity: Less or More
Ruling for grain sale when actual quantity differs from stipulation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that quantity is the essence (asl) in makilat and mawzunat to determine the buyer's and seller's rights when actual quantity differs from the stipulated amount.

Core Idea
Quantity is the essence, not a description – price adjusts proportionally.

When buying a heap of grain with a specified number of measures, what happens if you find less or more than agreed? The Hanafi school gives a clear answer based on whether quantity is part of the essence (asl) or merely a description (wasf). This lesson unpacks that distinction and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction type
Recognize that the sale is of a specific heap (sibratun) with a stipulated quantity (100 qafiz) and price (100 dirhams). The quantity is explicitly made part of the contract.
2
Understand the asl vs. wasf distinction
In Hanafi fiqh, for measurable (makilat) and weighable (mawzunat) goods, the quantity is the essence (asl) – the very substance of the sale. For cloth and land, length/area is a description (wasf). This difference determines the ruling.
The text explains: if cutting makes the item defective, the dimension is wasf; if not, it is asl.
3
Apply to the 'less' scenario
If the buyer finds less grain than stipulated, the subject matter has changed before completion (tafarruq al-safqah). The buyer has an option (khiyar): take the existing quantity at a proportionate price (e.g., 90 qafiz for 90 dirhams) or cancel the sale.
The reason: the contract was for 100 qafiz, and the buyer's consent was to that whole amount; receiving less breaks the consent.
4
Apply to the 'more' scenario
If the buyer finds more grain than stipulated, the excess belongs to the seller. The sale was for a specific quantity and does not include additional quantity, as the excess is also part of the essence, not a description that can be included by default.
The price remains 100 dirhams for 100 qafiz, and the seller retains the extra grain.
5
Generalize the principle
In all sales of goods where quantity is the essence (makilat, mawzunat, adadiyat mutaqaribah), the price is linked to quantity proportionally. For goods where dimension is a description (thawb, ard), a difference in length does not give an option unless it affects the value.
This principle is rooted in the nature of the commodity and the parties' intent.

زیادہ پایا تو زیادتی بائع کے لئے ہوگی کیونکہ مبیع مقدار معین پر واقع ہوئی ہے اور جو چیز مقدار معین پر واقع ہو وہ اس کے علاوہ کو شامل نہیں ہوتی الا یہ کہ وہ زائد از قبیلہ وصف ہو۔ اور مقدار معین پر جوزائد مقدار ہے وہ وصف نہیں ہے بلکہ اصل اور از قبیلہ مقدار ہے۔ اس لئے بیع اس زائد مقدار کو شامل نہ ہوگی اور جب بیع مقدار زائد کو شامل نہ ہوئی تو زیادتی بائع کے لئے ہوگی نہ کہ مشتری کے لئے۔ کیوں کہ مشتری کے لئے وہی چیز ہوتی ہے جس کو عقد بیع شامل ہوتا ہے۔
He said: Whoever buys a heap of grain on the condition that it is one hundred qafiz for one hundred dirhams, then finds it less: the buyer has the option: if he wishes he takes what is found at its share of the price, and if he wishes he cancels the sale because the transaction has become scattered for him before completion, so his consent to what is found is not complete. If he finds it more: the excess is for the seller because the sale occurred on a specific quantity, and quantity is not a description.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for a sale of grain where the actual quantity differs from the stipulated quantity. The key point is that in grain, quantity is considered the essence (asl) of the commodity, not merely a description (wasf). Therefore, the price is proportionate to the quantity. When the buyer finds less, he has the option (khiyar) to either take the lesser quantity at a proportionate price or cancel the sale entirely. This is because the contract was for a specific amount, and when the actual amount is less, the subject matter of the contract has changed, leading to tafarruq al-safqah (scattering of the transaction) before the contract was fully completed, thus the buyer's consent is not complete. If the buyer finds more, the excess belongs to the seller because the sale was for a specific quantity and does not include additional quantity, as the excess is also of the essence (asl) not a description. This ruling applies to measurable and weighable goods (makilat and mawzunat) where quantity is the asl. Note that the price corresponds to the asl, meaning an increase or decrease in quantity changes the price proportionally.

Key Terms
صبرة (sibratun): A heap of grain, usually referring to a pile of wheat or similar commodity.
قفيز (qafīz): A measure of capacity for grain, varying by region but standardized in fiqh texts.
صفقة (ṣafqatun): The transaction or deal; tafarruq al-safqah means the scattering of the transaction due to a change in the subject matter.
مقدار (miqdār): Quantity or measure; in this context, the specific amount of grain that is the essence (asl) of the sale.
وصف (wāṣif): Description or attribute; in this ruling, length is considered a description for cloth and land, not the essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He must take the 90 qafiz at full price.
B) He can take the 90 qafiz at 90 dirhams or cancel the sale.
C) He can take the entire heap at 100 dirhams.
D) He must cancel the sale.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales of measurable goods, quantity is the essence: deficiency gives the buyer a pro-rata option, and excess belongs to the seller.

Ruling on Sale with Stipulated Length: Deficiency or Excess in Cloth and Land
Ruling for sale with stipulated length when actual length is less or more

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling for a sale where the stipulated length differs from the actual length, identifying whether the length is a description (wasf) or essence (asl) and determining the buyer's options.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, length in cloth and land is a description; deficiency gives the buyer an option to take at full price or cancel, but never to reduce the price.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common scenario in sales: when a commodity (cloth or land) is bought with a specified length but found to be less or more. The Hanafi ruling hinges on the distinction between the essence (asl) and the description (wasf). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the buyer's option (khiyar) and avoiding the common error of demanding a proportionate price reduction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject matter and the stipulation
The buyer specifies the length (e.g., 10 cubits for cloth, 100 cubits for land) at the time of contract. This specification is a description (wasf) of the item, not its essence (asl).
2
Distinguish between asl and wasf in the contract
In Hanafi fiqh, the price (thaman) corresponds to the asl (substance) and not to the wasf (attribute). Therefore, a deficiency in the wasf does not reduce the price proportionally—the buyer must either accept the item at the full price or cancel the contract.
Compare with the sale of grain where quantity is asl, so price reduction is allowed.
3
Apply the ruling for deficient length
If the actual length is less than stipulated, the buyer has a khiyar (option): he may take the item with the full price or rescind the contract. He cannot demand a reduction in price because the deficiency is in a description.
The analogy with limbs of an animal: if a sold animal loses a limb before delivery, the buyer cannot reduce the price but can cancel.
4
Apply the ruling for excess length
If the actual length is more than stipulated, the excess belongs to the buyer, and the seller has no option. This is analogous to selling a defective item that turns out to be sound—the buyer gets the benefit.
The seller cannot claim compensation for the additional length.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن اشترى ثوبا على انه عشرة اذرع بعشرة او ارضاعلى انهامائة ذراع بمائة فوجدها اقل فالمشترى بالخيار ان شاء اخذها بجملة الثمن وان شاء ترك لان الذراع وصف فى الثوب الا ترى انه عبارة عن الطول والعرض والوصف لا يقابله شيء من الثمن كاطراف الحيوان فلهذا يا خذه بكل الثمن بخلاف الفصل الاول لان المقدار يقابله الثمن فلهذا يا خذه بحصته الا انه يتخير لفوات الوصف المذكور لتغير المعقود عليه فيختل الرضا وان وجدها أكثر من الذراع الذي سماه فهو للمشرى ولاخيار للبائع لانه صفة فكان بمنزلة ما اذا باعه معيبا فاذا هو سليم ترجمہ .... اور اگر کسی نے ایک کپڑا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ وہ دس گز ہے دس درہم کے عوض یا کوئی زمین اس شرط پر خریدی کہ وہ سوگز ہے سو درہم کے عوض پھر مشتری نے اس کو کم پایا تو اس کو اختیار ہے چاہے اس کو پورے شمن کے عوض لے لے اور اگر چاہے تو چھوڑ دے کیونکہ گز کپڑے میں ایک وصف ہے۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ گز طول و عرض کا نام ہے اور وصف کے مقابلہ میں شمن کا کوئی حصہ نہیں ہوتا جیسے حیوان کے ہاتھ پاؤں وغیرہ پس اسی وجہ سے اس کو کل ثمن کے عوض لے لے۔ برخلاف مسئلہ اول کے کیونکہ مقدار کے مقابلہ میں شمن ہوتا ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے اس کو اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض دے گا مگر یہ کہ مشتری کو اختیار ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ معقود علیہ کے متغیر ہونے کی وجہ سے وصف مذکور فوت ہو گیا ہے اس لئے مشتری کی رضا مندی مختل ہو جائے گی اور اگر مشتری نے اس کو ان گزوں سے زیادہ پایا جو بیان کئے ہیں تو وہ زائد مشتری کے لئے ہے اور بائع کو کوئی خیار نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ گز ایک صفت ہے پس وہ اس صورت کے مرتبہ میں ہوا کہ بائع نے ایک عیب دار چیز کو بیچا پھر وہ بے عیب نکلی۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے ایک کپڑا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ یہ دس گز دس درہم کے عوض ہیں یاز مین اس شرط پر خریدی کہ یہ سو گز سو درہم کے عوض ہیں۔ لیکن جب اس کو ناپ کر دیکھا تو وہ بیان کردہ گزوں سے کم نکلی ۔ پس ایسی صورت میں مشتری کو اختیار ہوگا۔ چاہے تو اس کو پورے شمن کے عوض لے لے اور چاہے بیع کو فسخ کر دے البتہ مشتری کو مقررہ چمن میں سے کچھ کم کرنے کا حق حاصل نہ ہوگا دلیل یہ ہے کہ کپڑے میں ذراع (گز) وصف ہوتا ہے چنانچہ آپ ملاحظہ فرمائیں کہ اگر طول و عرض کا نام ہے اور طول و عرض اوصاف کے قبیل سے ہیں۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ گز کپڑے اور زمین میں وصف ہے اور وصف کے مقابلہ میں شمن نہیں آتا ہے۔ یعنی اوصاف کے کم یا زیادہ ہونے سے من کم یا زیادہ نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے مشترکی اگر چاہے تو موجودہ زمین یا موجودہ کپڑے کو پورے شمن کے عوض لے لے اور اس کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے کسی نے ایک باندی خریدی پھر وہ باندی بائع کے قبضہ میں رہتے ہوئے ایک آنکھ سے نابینا ہوگئی تو مشتری کوشن میں سے کچھ کم کر دینے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ برخلاف مسئلہ اول کے کیونکہ اناج میں مقدار وصف نہیں ہے بلکہ اصل ہے اور اصل کے مقابلہ میں شمن آتا ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں مشتری اناج کی موجودہ مقدار کو اگر چاہے تو اس کے حصہ یمن کے عوض نے گا۔ بہر حال زمین اور کپڑے کے کم ہونے کی وجہ سے مشتری ثمن میں تو کمی نہیں کر سکتا البتہ اس کو نہ لینے کا اختیار ضرور ہوگا۔ کیوں کہ وصف
Whoever buys a cloth on the condition that it is ten cubits for ten dirhams, or land on the condition that it is one hundred cubits for one hundred dirhams, then finds it less: the buyer has the option, if he wishes he takes it with the full price, and if he wishes he leaves it, because the cubit is a description in the cloth; do you not see that it is an expression of length and width, and a description is not counterbalanced by any part of the price, like the limbs of an animal. Therefore he takes it with the full price, unlike the first section because the quantity is counterbalanced by the price, therefore he takes it at its share, except that he has an option due to the loss of the mentioned description because the subject matter has changed, so his consent is disturbed. And if he finds it more than the cubit which he mentioned, then it is for the buyer, and there is no option for the seller, because it is a description, so it is like the case where he sold a defective item and it turned out to be sound.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for a sale of cloth or land where the actual length differs from the stipulated length. The key point is that in cloth and land, length is considered a description (wasf), not the essence (asl). Therefore, the price is not proportionate to the length. When the buyer finds less, he has the option to either take the item at the full price (since the length is a description and does not reduce the price) or cancel the sale. He cannot demand a price reduction because descriptions are not counterbalanced by the price. The example given is like buying a slave girl who loses an eye while in the seller's possession: the buyer cannot reduce the price but can cancel. If the buyer finds more, the excess belongs to the buyer (since it is a description that is better), and the seller has no option. This is compared to the case where a seller sells a defective item and it turns out to be sound, so the buyer gets the benefit. This ruling contrasts with the previous grain case where quantity is the essence, so price is proportionate.

Key Terms
ذراع (dhirā'): A cubit, a unit of length used for measuring cloth and land, considered a description (wasf) in this context.
وصف (waṣf): Attribute or description; here, length is a description that does not affect the price proportionally but gives the buyer an option if missing.
ثمن (thaman): Price; in this ruling, the full price is paid because the description (length) does not counterbalance the price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person buys a cloth with the condition that it is 10 cubits for 10 dirhams. He finds it is only 8 cubits. What are his options according to Hanafi Fiqh?
A) He can take the cloth at a reduced price of 8 dirhams.
B) He can take the cloth at the full price of 10 dirhams or cancel the sale.
C) The excess 2 cubits belong to the seller.
D) He must take the cloth at full price with no option.

Key Takeaway
When a stipulated description (wasf) is deficient in a sale, the buyer cannot reduce the price but has the option to take the item at full price or cancel; if the description is excessive, the buyer benefits without extra payment.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Buyer's Option When Described Measurement Is Deficient or Excessive
Explains buyer's option for deficiency and seller's lack of option for excess

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a sold cloth or land is found to be less or more than the described cubits, and identify the reason based on the description (wasf) principle.

Core Idea
Deficiency in description gives buyer option to take all or leave; excess benefits buyer, seller has no claim.

This passage clarifies the difference between a description (wasf) and an essential quantity in sales. In Hanafi fiqh, when an item is sold with a specific cubit measurement, that measurement is treated as a description. Therefore, if the item falls short, the buyer cannot demand a proportional price reduction; instead, he must either accept the item at the full price or cancel the contract. Conversely, if the item exceeds the description, the excess belongs to the buyer and the seller has no right to additional payment. This ruling is derived through qiyas (analogy) to the sale of animal limbs and to defective goods that turn out sound.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? Sale of cloth/land with described cubits. When found less, buyer has option (khiyar) to take at full price or cancel. When found more, excess is buyer's, seller no option.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is rational (qiyas): the cubit is a description, not matched by any part of the price, analogous to animal limbs. Contrasted with grain case where quantity is essence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase: 'الوصف لا يقابله شيء من الثمن' (description is not matched by any part of the price). This is the illa.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
No inter-madhhab dispute mentioned. The contrasting grain case shows that for essential quantities, proportional reduction is allowed.
5
Evaluate the thamarah
Buyer cannot reduce price; only option to take all or cancel. Seller cannot increase price if more.

ومن اشترى ثوبا على انه عشرة اذرع بعشرة او ارضاعلى انهامائة ذراع بمائة فوجدها اقل فالمشترى بالخيار ان شاء اخذها بجملة الثمن وان شاء ترك لان الذراع وصف فى الثوب الا ترى انه عبارة عن الطول والعرض والوصف لا يقابله شيء من الثمن كاطراف الحيوان فلهذا يا خذه بكل الثمن بخلاف الفصل الاول لان المقدار يقابله الثمن فلهذا يا خذه بحصته الا انه يتخير لفوات الوصف المذكور لتغير المعقود عليه فيختل الرضا وان وجدها أكثر من الذراع الذي سماه فهو للمشرى ولاخيار للبائع لانه صفة فكان بمنزلة ما اذا باعه معيبا فاذا هو سليم

ترجمہ .... اور اگر کسی نے ایک کپڑا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ وہ دس گز ہے دس درہم کے عوض یا کوئی زمین اس شرط پر خریدی کہ وہ سوگز ہے سو درہم کے عوض پھر مشتری نے اس کو کم پایا تو اس کو اختیار ہے چاہے اس کو پورے شمن کے عوض لے لے اور اگر چاہے تو چھوڑ دے کیونکہ گز کپڑے میں ایک وصف ہے۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ گز طول و عرض کا نام ہے اور وصف کے مقابلہ میں شمن کا کوئی حصہ نہیں ہوتا جیسے حیوان کے ہاتھ پاؤں وغیرہ پس اسی وجہ سے اس کو کل ثمن کے عوض لے لے۔ برخلاف مسئلہ اول کے کیونکہ مقدار کے مقابلہ میں شمن ہوتا ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے اس کو اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض دے گا مگر یہ کہ مشتری کو اختیار ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ معقود علیہ کے متغیر ہونے کی وجہ سے وصف مذکور فوت ہو گیا ہے اس لئے مشتری کی رضا مندی مختل ہو جائے گی اور اگر مشتری نے اس کو ان گزوں سے زیادہ پایا جو بیان کئے ہیں تو وہ زائد مشتری کے لئے ہے اور بائع کو کوئی خیار نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ گز ایک صفت ہے پس وہ اس صورت کے مرتبہ میں ہوا کہ بائع نے ایک عیب دار چیز کو بیچا پھر وہ بے عیب نکلی۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے ایک کپڑا اس شرط پر خریدا کہ یہ دس گز دس درہم کے عوض ہیں یاز مین اس شرط پر خریدی کہ یہ سو گز سو درہم کے عوض ہیں۔ لیکن جب اس کو ناپ کر دیکھا تو وہ بیان کردہ گزوں سے کم نکلی ۔ پس ایسی صورت میں مشتری کو اختیار ہوگا۔ چاہے تو اس کو پورے شمن کے عوض لے لے اور چاہے بیع کو فسخ کر دے البتہ مشتری کو مقررہ چمن میں سے کچھ کم کرنے کا حق حاصل نہ ہوگا دلیل یہ ہے کہ کپڑے میں ذراع (گز) وصف ہوتا ہے چنانچہ آپ ملاحظہ فرمائیں کہ اگر طول و عرض کا نام ہے اور طول و عرض اوصاف کے قبیل سے ہیں۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ گز کپڑے اور زمین میں وصف ہے اور وصف کے مقابلہ میں شمن نہیں آتا ہے۔ یعنی اوصاف کے کم یا زیادہ ہونے سے من کم یا زیادہ نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے مشترکی اگر چاہے تو موجودہ زمین یا موجودہ کپڑے کو پورے شمن کے عوض لے لے اور اس کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے کسی نے ایک باندی خریدی پھر وہ باندی بائع کے قبضہ میں رہتے ہوئے ایک آنکھ سے نابینا ہوگئی تو مشتری کوشن میں سے کچھ کم کر دینے کا اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ برخلاف مسئلہ اول کے کیونکہ اناج میں مقدار وصف نہیں ہے بلکہ اصل ہے اور اصل کے مقابلہ میں شمن آتا ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں مشتری اناج کی موجودہ مقدار کو اگر چاہے تو اس کے حصہ یمن کے عوض نے گا۔ بہر حال زمین اور کپڑے کے کم ہونے کی وجہ سے مشتری ثمن میں تو کمی نہیں کر سکتا البتہ اس کو نہ لینے کا اختیار ضرور ہوگا۔ کیوں کہ وصف مذکور (ذراع) کے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے معقود علیہ متغیر ہو گیا ہے اور جب معقود علیہ متغیر ہو گیا ہے تو مشتری کی رضا مندی میں خلل واقع ہو گیا ہے اور مشتری کی رضا مندی مختل ہونے سے مشترکی کو اختیار ہوتا ہے کہ وہ بیع نافذ کرے یا نخ کرے۔ اور اگر زمین یا کپڑا مقررہ گروں سے زیادہ نکلا تو وہ زیادتی مشتری کے لئے ہوگی اور بائع کو کوئی اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ذراع (گز) ایک وصف ہے اور وصف کے مقابلہ میں شمن کا کوئی حصہ نہیں آتا ہے۔ اس لئے ذراع کے بڑھ جانے سے ثمن میں اضافہ نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور یہ ایسا ہے جیسے کسی نے ایک غلام نابینا کہ [؟] کہ خریدا اور اسی حساب سے شمن مقر رکیا پھر بعد میں معلوم ہوا کہ وہ تو نابینا ہے۔ پس اس وصف بصارت کے بڑھ جانے سے ثمن میں اضافہ نہیں ہوگا۔ اور بائع کوکوئی اختیار نہ ہوگا۔
The one who buys a cloth on the condition that it is ten cubits for ten [dirhams], or land on the condition that it is one hundred cubits for one hundred [dirhams], and finds it less, then the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he takes it for the entire price, and if he wishes, he leaves it. Because the cubit is a description in the cloth; do you not see that it expresses length and breadth, and a description is not matched by any part of the price, like the limbs of an animal. Therefore, he takes it for the entire price, unlike the first chapter [grain case], because quantity is matched by the price, so he takes it for its share, except that he has an option due to the loss of the mentioned description, because the object of contract has changed, so consent is impaired. And if he finds it more than the cubit which he specified, then it is for the buyer, and there is no option for the seller, because it is a description, so it is like the case when he sold a defective item and it turned out to be sound.

Translation: And if someone bought a cloth on the condition that it is ten cubits for ten dirhams, or bought a land on the condition that it is one hundred cubits for one hundred dirhams, then the buyer found it less, then he has the option: if he wishes, he takes it for the full price, and if he wishes, he leaves it. Because the cubit in the cloth is a description. Do you not see that the cubit is a term for length and breadth, and against the description no part of the price is allocated, like the hands and feet of an animal. Therefore, he takes it for the entire price. Contrary to the first issue, because quantity is matched by the price, so he takes it for its share of the price, but the buyer will have an option. Because due to the change in the object of contract, the mentioned description is lost, thus the buyer's consent becomes impaired. And if the buyer found it more than the cubits that were mentioned, then the excess is for the buyer, and the seller has no option. Because the cubit is a quality, so it is like the case where the seller sold a defective item and it turned out to be sound.

Explanation: The issue is that a person bought a cloth on the condition that it is ten cubits for ten dirhams, or land on the condition that it is one hundred cubits for one hundred dirhams. But when he measured it, he found it less than the stated cubits. In such a case, the buyer has an option: if he wishes, he takes it for the full price, and if he wishes, he rescinds the contract. However, the buyer does not have the right to reduce the agreed price. The proof is that the cubit in the cloth is a description. Thus, you may note that if it is a term for length and breadth, and length and breadth belong to the category of descriptions. So it is known that the cubit in cloth and land is a description, and against a description no price is allocated; meaning the price does not increase or decrease with the increase or decrease of descriptions. Therefore, the buyer, if he wishes, takes the existing land or existing cloth for the full price. An example of this is if someone bought a slave girl and then that slave girl became blind in one eye while in the seller's possession; the buyer does not have the option to reduce the price. Contrary to the first issue, because in grain, quantity is not a description but the essence, and against the essence the price is allocated. So in that case, the buyer takes the existing quantity of grain, if he wishes, for its share of the price. In any case, due to the deficiency in land or cloth, the buyer cannot reduce the price, but he certainly has the option not to take it. Because due to the loss of the mentioned description (cubit), the object of contract has changed, and when the object of contract has changed, the buyer's consent is impaired, and due to the impaired consent, the buyer has the option to execute or cancel the sale. And if the land or cloth is found more than the stated cubits, then the excess is for the buyer, and the seller has no option. Because the cubit is a description, and against a description no part of the price is allocated. Therefore, with the increase of cubits, the price will not be increased. This is like when someone bought a slave who is blind, and fixed the price accordingly, then later it became known that he is not blind. Then due to the increase of the description of sight, the price will not be increased, and the seller has no option.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the sale of a cloth or land where the seller describes a specific number of cubits (e.g., ten cubits for ten dirhams). When the buyer finds the actual measurement less than stated, the text explains that the buyer has a choice: either take the item at the full price or cancel the sale. The key reason is that the cubit is considered a description (wasf) of the item, like the length and breadth. In Hanafi fiqh, a description does not correspond to any portion of the price; rather, the price is for the essence of the item. Therefore, the buyer cannot demand a proportional reduction in price. Instead, he must either accept the item as is with the full price or reject it entirely. This is contrasted with a prior case involving grain, where quantity is the essence and thus price reduction is allowed. If the item is found to be more than described, the excess belongs to the buyer and the seller has no option, because the description being better does not give the seller any right to increase the price. The text draws an analogy to selling a defective item that turns out to be sound; the seller cannot claim extra. The commentary uses examples like a slave girl losing an eye or a blind slave turning out sighted to illustrate the principle.

Key Terms
ذراع (dhirāʿ): A unit of length (cubit) used to describe cloth or land; in this context, it is considered a description (wasf) of the item.
وصف (waṣf): An attribute or quality of the object of sale; here, the cubit is a description of length and breadth.
ثمن (thaman): The price paid in a sale; in this context, it is for the substance of the item, not its description.
مشترى (mushtarī): The buyer in a sale contract.
بائع (bāʾiʿ): The seller in a sale contract.
خيار (khiyār): The option or right to choose to uphold or cancel the contract; here the buyer has the option due to deficiency in description.
معقود عليه (maʿqūd ʿalayhi): The object of the contract, i.e., the item being sold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person buys a cloth described as 10 cubits for 10 dirhams, and finds it to be only 8 cubits, what is the buyer's right according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) The buyer may take the cloth at a reduced price of 8 dirhams.
B) The buyer must take the cloth at the full price of 10 dirhams.
C) The buyer may either take the cloth at the full price or cancel the sale.
D) The buyer may demand compensation from the seller for the deficiency.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales law, a described dimension (like cubits) is a description, not an essential quantity; deficiency gives the buyer an option to take all or leave, but no price reduction; excess benefits the buyer without additional cost.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Ruling When Each Cubit is Priced Individually and Measurement Differs
Explains buyer's option when each cubit has a separate price and total length differs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the buyer's options when each cubit is individually priced and apply the rule that the cubit becomes an essence.

Core Idea
When each cubit has its own price, it becomes an essence; buyer may take proportionally or cancel if less, and take all at per-unit price or cancel if more.

This lesson builds on the prior ruling where the cubit was a mere description. Here, the seller explicitly prices each cubit separately, transforming the cubit from a subsidiary description into an independent object of sale. The legal consequence is that the buyer gains options when the actual quantity differs from what was stated, protecting him from being forced to pay for undelivered goods or to accept excess without consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the operative phrase
Focus on the seller's statement 'each cubit for one dirham.' This phrase allocates a separate price to each unit, distinguishing this case from a simple bulk sale.
The phrase 'كل ذراع بدرهم' is key.
2
Understand the transformation from description to essence
Because each cubit receives its own price, it is no longer a mere description of the total but becomes an essence (asl). The price is matched to each unit, just as it would be for separate garments.
The text analogizes each cubit to a separate piece of cloth.
3
Apply the rule when quantity is less
If the cloth is shorter than stated, the buyer may take the actual length at the proportionate price (e.g., 90 cubits for 90 dirhams) or cancel the sale. He cannot be forced to pay the full price for less.
Proportionate price = actual cubits × unit price.
4
Apply the rule when quantity is more
If the cloth is longer, the buyer may take the entire cloth at the per-unit price (paying more) or cancel the sale. The increase in price is binding if he takes the excess, because each cubit is an essence.
No option to take only the stated quantity at the original price.
5
Understand the rationale
The ruling is based on qiyas: the separate pricing makes each cubit analogous to an independent item, so the buyer's acceptance is tied to each unit. This prevents injustice to either party.
The proof is that the price is allocated to each cubit individually.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سوگز سو درہم کے بدلے اور ہرگز ایک درہم کے بدلے، کم یا زیادہ نکلیں تو بیع کا حکم

ولوقال بعتكها على انها مائة ذراع بمائة درهم كل ذرائع بدرهم فوجد هانا قصة فالمشترى بالخياران شاء اخذها بحصتها من الثمن وان شاء ترك لان الوصف وان كان تابعا لكنه صارا صلا بافراده بذكر الثمن فنزل كل ذراع بمنزلة ثوب وهذا لانه لو اخذه بكل الثمن لم يكن آخذا لكل ذرائع بدر هم وان وجدها زائدة فهو بالخيار ان شاء اخذ الجميع كل ذراع بدرهم وان شاء فسخ البيع لانه ان حصل له الزيادة في الذراع تلزمه زيادة الثمن فكان نفعایشو به ضرر فيتخير وانما يلزمه الزيادة لما بينا انه صار اصلا ولواخذه بالاقل لم يكن اخذا بالمشروط

ترجمہ اور اگر بائع نے کہا کہ میں نے تجھ کو یہ کپڑا اس شرط پر فروخت کیا کہ سوگز سو درہم کے عوض بحساب ہر گز ایک درہم کے عوض ہے پھر مشتری نے اس کو کم پایا تو مشتری کو اختیار ہے کہ چاہے تو موجودہ کو اس کے حصہ یمن کے عوض لے لے اور اگر چاہے چھوڑ دے کیونکہ ذراع کا وصف اگر چہ تابع تھا لیکن اس کا شن علیحدہ ذکر کرنے کی وجہ سے وہ اصل بن گیا۔ پس ہرگز علیحدہ کپڑے کے مرتبہ میں اتار لیا گیا اور یہ حکم اس لئے ہے کہ اگر موجودہ کو کل شمن کے عوض لے گا تو وہ ہر ذراع ایک درہم کے حساب سے لینے والا نہ ہوگا ۔ اور اگر مشتری نے اس کو زائد پایا تو اس کو اختیار ہے کہ اگر چاہے پورے کپڑے کو بحساب کل ذراع بدر ہم لیلے اور اگر چاہے بیچ مسخ کر دے۔ اس لئے کہ اگر اس کو گزروں میں زیادتی حاصل ہوئی تو شمن کی زیادتی بھی اس پر لازم ہوئی ہے۔ پس یہ ایسا نفع ہے جس کے ساتھ ضر ر ملا ہوا ہے۔ اس لئے مشتری کو اختیار ہوگا۔ اور مشتری پر زیادتی شمن اس دلیل کی وجہ سے لازم ہوئی ہے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے کہ ذراع اصل ہو گیا اور اگر اس کو کم داموں کے عوض لے گا تو کل ذراع بدرہم کی شرط کے موافق لینے والا ہوگا۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے اس شرط کے ساتھ کپڑ ایچا کہ سوگ کا تھان سو درہم کے عوض بحساب ایک گز ایک درہم کے عوض ہے پھر اس تھان کو ناپ کر دیکھا تو وہ سو گز سے کم نکلا ۔ پس ایسی صورت میں مشتری کو اختیار ہے چاہے تو موجودہ کپڑے کو اس کے حصہ ثمن کے عوض لے لے اور اگر چاہے تو چھوڑ دے حصہ مشن کے عوش لینے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ذراع اگر چہ تابع اور وصف ہے۔ لیکن کل ذراع بدرہم کے ذریعہ چونکہ ہر ذراع کا شمن علیحدہ علیحدہ ذکر کیا گیا ہے اس لئے ذراع اصل ہو گیا کیونکہ ثمن کا کسی چیز کے مقابلہ میں آنا اس چیز کے اصل ہونے کی علامت ہوتی ہے پس ہر ذراع کے مقابلہ میں بدرہم کے ذریعہ من بیان کر دینے کی وجہ سے ہر ذراع بمنزلہ
Ruling on sale when it is one hundred cubits for one hundred dirhams, each cubit for one dirham, and it turns out less or more.

And if he says, 'I sold it to you on the condition that it is one hundred cubits for one hundred dirhams, each cubit for one dirham,' and he finds it less, then the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he takes it for its share of the price, and if he wishes, he leaves it. Because the description, although it was subsidiary, became an essence by mentioning the price separately, so each cubit is treated like a separate garment. This is because if he took it for the entire price, he would not be taking each cubit for one dirham. And if he finds it more, then he has the option: if he wishes, he takes all, each cubit for one dirham, and if he wishes, he cancels the sale. Because if he gains an increase in cubits, he is obligated to an increase in price, so it is a benefit mixed with harm, so he has an option. The increase in price is obligatory because, as we stated, it has become an essence. And if he took it for less, he would not be taking in accordance with the condition.

Translation: And if the seller said, 'I sold you this cloth on the condition that it is one hundred cubits for one hundred dirhams, at the rate of each cubit for one dirham,' then the buyer finds it less, then the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he takes the existing for its share of the price, and if he wishes, he leaves it. Because the description of the cubit, although it was subsidiary, became an essence due to mentioning its price separately. Therefore, each cubit is treated as a separate cloth. This ruling is because if he takes the existing for the whole price, he would not be taking each cubit for the rate of one dirham. And if the buyer finds it more, then he has the option: if he wishes, he takes the entire cloth at the rate of all cubits for one dirham each, and if he wishes, he rescinds the sale. Because if he gains an increase in cubits, an increase in price also becomes binding on him. So this is a benefit accompanied by harm. Therefore, the buyer has an option. And the increase in price is binding on the buyer due to the proof we mentioned: that the cubit has become an essence. And if he takes it for a lower price, he would not be taking in accordance with the condition of each cubit for one dirham.

Explanation: The issue is that a person bought a cloth with the condition that a one-hundred-cubit piece is for one hundred dirhams at the rate of one cubit for one dirham. Then when he measured that piece, he found it less than one hundred cubits. In such a case, the buyer has the option: if he wishes, he takes the existing cloth for its share of the price, and if he wishes, he leaves it. The proof for taking at the share of the price is that the cubit, although it is subsidiary and a description, due to mentioning each cubit's price separately through 'each cubit for one dirham', the cubit became an essence, because the price being matched to something is an indication of that thing being an essence. Thus, because the price was stated for each cubit separately, each cubit is treated like...

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding a sale where the seller states a total length and total price but also specifies a per-unit price ('each cubit for one dirham'). The Hanafi ruling here differs from the previous case. Because the per-unit price makes each cubit an independent object of sale (asl), rather than a mere description. Therefore, if the actual length is less, the buyer may take the cloth at a proportionate price (i.e., paying only for the actual cubits at the agreed per-unit rate) or cancel the sale. This is because the cubit is now treated like a separate item. If the length is more, the buyer has the option to take all at the per-unit price (thus paying more) or cancel the sale. The logic is that an increase in cubits brings an increased price obligation, which is a benefit mixed with harm, so the buyer has an option. The text explains that the cubit becomes an essence because the price is allocated to each unit, similar to selling multiple separate garments. The buyer cannot simply take the excess without paying; he must either pay the full increased price or cancel the contract.

Key Terms
ذراع (dhirāʿ): A cubit; in this context, when priced individually, it becomes an essence (asl) rather than a description.
وصف (waṣf): Description; initially subsidiary but can become essence when priced separately.
اصل (aṣl): Essence or substance; here, when each cubit has a separate price, it is treated as an essence (like a separate item).
ثمن (thaman): Price; allocated to each cubit individually in this case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sale where the seller says 'This cloth is 100 cubits for 100 dirhams, each cubit for one dirham,' and the cloth is found to be 90 cubits, what are the buyer's options according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) The buyer must take the cloth at the full price of 100 dirhams.
B) The buyer may take the cloth at a reduced price of 90 dirhams or cancel the sale.
C) The buyer has no option; the seller can demand the full price.
D) The buyer may take the cloth at any price he chooses.

Key Takeaway
When each unit of a sold item has its own price, the unit becomes an independent essence, giving the buyer an option to take proportionally or cancel if quantity is less, and to take all at unit price or cancel if quantity is more.
