بیع فاسد ہوگی جبکہ کسی نے کھڑی کھیتی کو خریدا ہو اور پکنے کے وقت تک کھیتی زمین میں چھوڑنے کی شرط ہو۔ دلیل سابق میں گزر چکی کہ یہ شرط مقتضا عقد کے خلاف اور صفقہ فی صفقہ بھی لازم آتا ہے۔ یہاں ایک سوال ہے وہ یہ کہ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ درخت پر بالعوض یا بلا عوض پھلوں کو چھوڑنے کی شرط لگانے کی صورت میں صفقة فی صفقة لازم آتا ہے۔ حالانکہ یہ غلط ہے کیونکہ درختوں کو نہ اجارہ پر دینا جائز ہے اور نہ عاریہ دینا جائز ہے۔ پس جب درختوں کا اجارہ اور اعارہ ناجائز ہے تو یہ صفقة ہی نہ ہوگی اور جب یہ صفقة نہیں ہے تو صفقة فی صفقة کہاں سے لازم آئے گا؟ ہاں زراعت کی صورت میں صفقة فی صفقة لازم آئے گا کیونکہ زمین کا اجارہ اور اعارہ دونوں جائز ہیں۔ اب حاصل یہ ہوا کہ پھلوں کو درخت پر چھوڑنے کی شرط کے ساتھ فساد بیع اس لیے ہے کہ یہ شرط مقتضائے عقد کے خلاف ہے۔ اور کھیتی کو زمین میں چھوڑنے کی شرط کے ساتھ دو وجہوں سے بیع فاسد ہے: ایک مقتضائے عقد کے خلاف ہونے کی وجہ سے، دوم صفقة فی صفقة کی وجہ سے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر پھلوں کی بڑھاور پوری ہوگئی یعنی ان کو جس قدر بڑھنا تھا اور موٹا ہونا تھا وہ ہو چکا اب ان کے حجم میں کوئی اضافہ متوقع نہیں ہے تو ایسی صورت میں اگر پھلوں کو اس شرط کے ساتھ خریدا کہ پکنے تک درخت پر چھوڑے رکھے گا تو شیخین کے نزدیک اس صورت میں بھی بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ شرط مقتضائے عقد کے خلاف ہے اور مقتضائے عقد کے خلاف شرط لگانے سے بیع فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس لیے اس صورت میں بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ اور امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ لوگوں کے تعامل کی وجہ سے استحساناً اس صورت میں بیع جائز ہے۔ اس پر فتویٰ ہے۔ ہاں اگر پھلوں کی بڑھاور پوری نہیں ہوئی بلکہ ان کے حجم میں اضافہ متوقع ہے تو شرط ترک کے ساتھ بالاتفاق بیع جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں جزء معدوم کی شرط ہے اور یہ وہ جز ہے جو زمین یا درخت کی قوت سے پیدا ہوگا اور یہ جز عقد بیع کے بعد بائع کی ملک سے پیدا ہوا ہے تو گویا مشتری نے موجود اور معدوم کو ملا کر خریدا ہے۔ اور معدوم اور موجود کو ملا کر خریدنے سے بیع فاسد ہوتی ہے۔ اس لیے اس صورت میں بیع فاسد ہوگی۔
Chapter of Sales. (54) Ashraf al-Hidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Eight. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (say invalid) for what we stated, and Muhammad deemed it permissible by istihsan due to custom, unlike when the (fruit's) growth has not reached its full size, because in that case there is a condition involving a non-existent part, which is that which increases by means of the earth or the tree. Translation: And if the buyer stipulates that he will leave them on the trees, then the sale is invalid. Because this condition is such that the contract does not require it, and it is occupying the property of another, or it is one transaction within another transaction, and that in the sale is a loan or a lease. And similarly, with the condition of leaving the crop in the land, for the reason we stated. And similarly according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf when the fruit has reached its full size, for the proof we stated. And Imam Muhammad deemed it permissible by istihsan due to custom. Contrary to the case when the fruit's growth has not reached its full size, because in that there is a condition of a non-existent part, and that is what will come into being from the strength of the earth or the tree. Explanation: The issue is that if someone says, 'I bought the fruit of this tree on condition that I will leave it on the tree until ripening time,' then this sale is invalid. The proof is that this condition is contrary to the requirement of the contract. Because the contract requires that the object of sale be delivered to the buyer and the buyer separate the object from the seller's ownership. This does not happen with this condition; rather, the buyer occupies the seller's property (the trees) with his own property (the fruit). So due to stipulating a condition contrary to the requirement of the contract, the sale becomes invalid. The second proof is that stipulating the condition of leaving the fruit on the tree necessitates one transaction within another. Because leaving the fruit on the tree is either for compensation or for free. If for compensation, i.e., the buyer fixed rent for leaving the fruit on the tree, then a lease enters into the sale. If for free, i.e., the buyer did not fix any rent, then a loan (ariyah) enters into the sale. The Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited a transaction within a transaction. Therefore, with this condition the sale is invalid. Similarly, this sale is invalid when someone buys standing crop and stipulates leaving it in the land until ripening time. The proof has passed earlier that this condition is contrary to the requirement of the contract and also necessitates a transaction within a transaction. Here there is a question: the author of al-Hidayah said that stipulating leaving the fruit on the tree with or without compensation necessitates a transaction within a transaction. But this is incorrect because it is not permissible to lease trees nor to loan them. When leasing and loaning trees are not permissible, then there is no transaction at all, and when there is no transaction, how can there be a transaction within a transaction? Yes, in the case of agriculture, a transaction within a transaction does occur because leasing and loaning land are both permissible. So the result is that the invalidity of the sale with the condition of leaving fruit on the tree is because this condition is contrary to the requirement of the contract. And the sale with the condition of leaving the crop in the land is invalid for two reasons: first because it is contrary to the requirement of the contract, second because of a transaction within a transaction. The author of al-Hidayah says: if the fruit's growth has reached its full size, i.e., it has grown as much as it should and has become thick, and no further increase in volume is expected, then even in this case, according to the two elders (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the sale is invalid. The proof is that this condition is contrary to the requirement of the contract, and stipulating a condition contrary to the requirement of the contract renders the sale invalid. So in this case the sale is invalid. And Imam Muhammad said that due to people's practice (ta'amul), by istihsan, the sale is permissible in this case. The fatwa is upon this. Yes, if the fruit's growth has not reached its full size, i.e., an increase in volume is expected, then with the condition of leaving it, the sale is not permissible by consensus. Because in this case there is a condition of a non-existent part, and this part will come into being from the strength of the earth or the tree, and this part comes into being after the contract of sale from the seller's ownership. So it is as if the buyer bought the existing and the non-existing together. And buying the non-existing and the existing together renders the sale invalid. Therefore, in this case the sale will be invalid.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of fruit with a condition that the fruit be left on the tree until ripening. The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the ruling is given by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two elders) that the sale is invalid (fasid) because the condition is contrary to the requirement of the contract (muqtada al-'aqd) and also constitutes a transaction within a transaction (safqataani fi safqah), which is prohibited. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, however, deems it permissible by istihsan due to custom (ta'amul), and this is the position upon which fatwa is given. The passage clarifies that this permissibility applies only when the fruit has reached its full size (mutanahi al-'uzm), because then the condition does not involve a non-existent part (juz' ma'dum). If the fruit has not reached full size, the sale is invalid by consensus because it involves selling a non-existent part along with an existing one, which is prohibited. The commentary also addresses a potential objection: the reasoning of safqatani fi safqah might not apply to trees because leasing or loaning trees is not permissible, but it applies to land for crops. Thus, the primary reason for invalidity in the fruit case is the condition being contrary to the contract's requirement. The passage follows the order: statement of ruling, proof from contract requirement, proof from prohibition of transaction within transaction, objection and response, then the ikhtilaf regarding full-grown fruit with the tarjih (preferred opinion) being Imam Muhammad's view.

Key Terms
مقتضی عقد (muqtada al-'aqd): The legal requirement or effect of a contract; what the contract inherently demands.
صفقة في صفقة (safqah fi safqah): A transaction within a transaction; combining two different contracts (like sale and lease) in one deal.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from strict qiyas in favor of a ruling that is more suitable due to custom, necessity, or equity.
جزء معدوم (juz' ma'dum): A non-existent part; here referring to the future growth of fruit that is not yet in existence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) opinion in the Hanafi school, when is the sale of fruit with a condition to leave it on the tree valid?
A) When the fruit has not yet reached full size and is expected to grow further.
B) When the fruit has reached full size (mutanahi al-'uzm) and no further increase is expected.
C) Only if the seller explicitly gives permission after the sale.
D) It is never valid under any condition.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the sale of fruit with a condition to leave it on the tree is valid (mufta bihi) when the fruit is fully grown, by virtue of istihsan based on custom; otherwise, it is invalid by consensus.

Increase in Fruit Left on Tree: Charity Required if Without Permission
Ruling on increase of fruit when left on tree without condition, with permission or without

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on fruit increase when left on the seller's tree without permission, distinguishing between increase in substance and change in condition.

Core Idea
Increase from another's property without permission must be given in charity; only real growth, not ripening, triggers the obligation.

When a buyer leaves fruit on the seller's tree after purchase, any increase may be lawful or require charity depending on permission and the type of increase. This lesson unpacks the two scenarios and the critical distinction between substantial growth and mere change in condition. We will also explore the analogy to usurped property that forms the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
First, determine whether the buyer left the fruit with or without the seller's permission. This is the key variable affecting the ruling.
The passage explicitly states two cases: with permission (increase lawful) and without permission (increase charitied).
2
Check the growth stage of the fruit
The obligation to give charity only applies if the fruit was left before reaching full size (qabl mutanahi al-'uzm). After full size, no charity is required.
Full size means the fruit has stopped growing in volume; subsequent changes are only qualitative.
3
Calculate the increase in value
When charity is required, the buyer must estimate the market value before full size and after full size. The difference is the amount to be given in charity.
This is a practical method to determine the increase attributable to the prohibited use.
4
Understand the legal reason for charity
The increase is obtained through a prohibited means (jihah mahzurah) because using someone else's trees without permission is akin to usurpation (ghasb). Therefore, the increase must be purified by charity.
This is a qiyas to the ruling on benefiting from usurped property.
5
Apply the exception for change in condition
After full size, changes like ripening, taste, and color are not considered real increases (ziyada fi al-dhat) but merely a change of condition (taghayyur hal). Hence, no charity is required.
This exception provides clarity: only real growth, not natural maturation, triggers the charity obligation.

پھل مطلقاً خریدے پھر بائع کی اجازت سے یا بغیر اجازت کے پھل درختوں پر چھوڑنے کا حکم

ولو اشتراها مطلقا وتركها باذن البائع طاب له الفضل وان تركها بغير اذنه تصدق بما زاد في ذاته لحصوله بجهة محظورة وان تركها بعد ماتنا هي عظمها لم يتصدق بشيء لان هذا تغير حالة لا تحقيق زيادة .
ترجمہ: اور اگر اس نے پھلوں کو مطلقاً خریدا اور بائع کی اجازت سے ان کو (درختوں پر) چھوڑا تو پھلوں کے اندر جو زیادتی ہو وہ مشتری کے لیے حلال ہوگی۔ اور اگر بائع کی اجازت کے بغیر ان کو چھوڑا تو جو کچھ پھلوں کی ذات میں اضافہ ہوا ہو اس کو صدقہ کر دے کیونکہ یہ زیادتی جهت ممنوعہ حاصل ہوتی ہے۔ اور اگر ان کی بڑھاور پوری ہونے کے بعد ان کو (بغیر اجازت کے) چھوڑا ہے تو کچھ صدقہ نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ یہ حالت کا تغیر ہے نہ کہ جسم کے اندر زیادتی۔
تشریح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر تم ہی عظم سے پہلے پھل خریدے اور درختوں پر چھوڑنے کی شرط نہیں کی لیکن اس کے باوجود درختوں پر چھوڑے رکھا تو اس کی دو صورتیں ہیں: یا تو ان کو بائع کی اجازت سے چھوڑا ہوگا یا بغیر اجازت کے چھوڑا ہوگا۔ پہلی صورت میں وہ اضافہ جو اس مدت میں پھلوں کے اندر ہوا ہے مشتری کے لیے حلال ہوگا۔ اور دوسری صورت میں اس زیادتی کا صدقہ کردے۔ اس کی صورت یہ ہے کہ تقاری عظم سے پہلے کی قیمت کا اندازہ کرالے اور پھر تنا ہی معظم کے بعد قیمت کا اندازہ کرائے۔ دونوں فرق ہے۔ مثلاً پہلے ایک ہزار روپے قیمت ہے اور تقاہی عظم کے بعد پندرہ سو روپے قیمت ہوگئی تو یہ پانچ سو روپے جو عقد بیع کے بعد پھلوں کو درختوں پر بغیر بائع کی اجازت کے چھوڑنے کی وجہ سے بڑھے ہیں ان کا صدقہ کرنا واجب ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس زیادتی کا حصول حرام طریقہ سے ہوا ہے بایں طور کہ بغیر مالک کی اجازت کے اس کی زمین اور درختوں سے نفع اٹھانا، غصب کی ہوئی زمین اور غصب کئے ہوئے درختوں سے نفع اٹھانا ہے۔ شکے منصوبہ سے نفع اٹھانا ممنوع اور ناجائز ہے۔ اس لیے اس زیادتی کا صدقہ کرنا واجب ہے۔ اور اگر تنا ہی عظم کے بعد بغیر بائع کی اجازت کے پھلوں کو درختوں پر چھوڑا ہو تو کسی چیز کا صدقہ کرنا واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ متناہی عظم کے بعد پھلوں کے حجم اور ان کی ذات میں کوئی اضافہ نہیں ہوگا بلکہ صرف پھلوں کی حالت میں تغیر پیدا ہوا کیونکہ تناہی عظم کے بعد پھلوں میں تین باتیں پیدا ہوتی ہیں: ایک پھلوں کا پکنا، دوسرا ذائقہ، تیسرا رنگ۔ ان تینوں چیزوں کا حصول نہ زمین سے ہوتا ہے نہ درخت سے بلکہ پھلوں کا پکنا آفتاب کا کام ہے اور ان میں رنگ بھرنا چاند کا عمل ہے۔
Ruling on fruit purchased absolutely, then left on trees with or without the seller's permission. And if he purchased them absolutely and left them with the seller's permission, then the increase is lawful for him. And if he left them without his permission, he should give in charity whatever increased in its substance because it was obtained through a prohibited means. And if he left them after they had reached their full size, he should not give anything in charity because this is a change of condition, not a real increase. Translation: And if he purchased the fruits absolutely and left them (on the trees) with the seller's permission, then whatever increase occurs in the fruits will be lawful for the buyer. And if he left them without the seller's permission, then whatever increase occurred in the substance of the fruits, he should give it in charity, because this increase is obtained through a prohibited means. And if he left them after their growth had reached full size, then he should not give anything in charity, because this is a change of condition, not an increase in the substance. Explanation: The issue is that if he purchased the fruit before reaching full size and did not stipulate the condition of leaving them on the trees, but nevertheless left them on the trees, then there are two possibilities: either he left them with the seller's permission or without. In the first case, the increase that occurred in the fruits during that period is lawful for the buyer. In the second case, he should give that increase in charity. The method is that he should estimate the price before full size and then estimate the price after full size. There is a difference. For example, the price was one thousand rupees before, and after full size it became fifteen hundred rupees, so these five hundred rupees, which increased due to leaving the fruit on the trees without the seller's permission after the contract of sale, must be given in charity. The proof is that this increase was obtained through a prohibited means, i.e., benefiting from someone else's land and trees without permission is like benefiting from usurped land and trees. Benefiting from a usurped property is prohibited and impermissible. Therefore, it is obligatory to give this increase in charity. And if he left the fruit after full size without the seller's permission, then it is not obligatory to give anything in charity, because after full size, there is no increase in the volume or substance of the fruit; rather, only a change in condition occurs. After full size, three things occur in the fruit: ripening, taste, and color. The occurrence of these three is not from the earth or the tree; rather, the ripening is the work of the sun, and the coloring is the work of the moon.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the increase in fruit when the buyer leaves it on the tree without any stipulation. The passage first states the ruling: if the buyer leaves the fruit with the seller's permission, any increase is lawful. If without permission, the increase must be given in charity. However, if the fruit has already reached full size (mutanahi al-'uzm) before being left, then no charity is required because the change is only in quality (ripening, taste, color), not in substance. The commentary explains the method for calculating the increase: estimate the value before full size and after full size, and the difference is the increase that must be given in charity. The proof provided is that benefiting from the seller's trees without permission is akin to benefiting from a usurper's property, which is prohibited (haram). Therefore, the increase is tainted and must be purified by giving it in charity. This ruling applies to fruit that is still growing; once growth has ceased, no charity is needed because the change is not an increase in substance. The passage follows a clear structure: statement of the ruling (matn) followed by explanation (sharh) with example and reasoning.

Key Terms
تصدق (tasaddaqa): To give in charity; here it means giving the value of the increase to charity to purify the tainted property.
تغير حالة (taghayyur hal): Change of condition; here referring to qualitative changes like ripening and coloring, as opposed to substantial increase (ziyada fi al-dhat).
جهة محظورة (jihah mahzurah): A prohibited means; here the benefit derived from using the seller's property without permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When must a buyer give the increase in fruit value to charity?
A) When he leaves the fruit on the tree with the seller’s permission before full size.
B) When he leaves the fruit on the tree without the seller’s permission after full size.
C) When he leaves the fruit on the tree without the seller’s permission before full size.
D) In all cases when he leaves the fruit on the tree.

Key Takeaway
Charity is wajib only for the increase in substance of fruit left without permission before full size; after full size, or with permission, no charity is required.

Selling Fruit with a Condition to Leave on the Tree
Intra-Hanafi dispute on condition of leaving fruit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling fruit with a condition to leave it on the tree, distinguish between the default fasid view and Imam Muhammad's jayiz view, and identify the crucial condition that makes the sale valid or invalid.

Core Idea
Imam Muhammad's istihsan allows a conditional sale if growth is complete, overriding the default fasid ruling.

In Hanafi sales law, a contract that includes a condition involving a future, non-existent part is generally fasid (defective). However, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani made an exception for the common practice of buying fruit with the condition that it remains on the tree after the sale. This lesson unpacks this dispute, its basis in istihsan, and the decisive factor of whether the fruit's growth is complete. Understanding this helps you grasp how custom (ta'amul) can override strict analogy in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the default ruling and its reasoning
Identify the base position: a sale with a condition to leave fruit on the tree is fasid because it involves buying a non-existent part (juz' ma'dum) that will arise after the contract from the seller's property.
This is the ruling of the earlier Hanafi scholars (likely Abu Hanifa or Sahibayn).
2
Present Imam Muhammad's view and its basis
Imam Muhammad holds the sale valid (jayiz) using istihsan, relying on people's customary practice (ta'amul). He considers the condition acceptable when the fruit's growth is complete.
The fatwa is on Imam Muhammad's view.
3
Identify the boundary condition
If the fruit's growth is incomplete and further increase is expected, then even Imam Muhammad agrees the sale is invalid by consensus. Here the non-existent part is not inseparable.
This is the point of agreement.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: when growth is complete, the buyer keeps the fruit; if growth is incomplete, the sale fails and the contract is fasid.
Only the condition of leaving matters; the underlying fruit must be fully grown.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
For fatwa, adopt Imam Muhammad's position: the sale is valid with the condition if the fruit's growth is complete.
This is the operative ruling per the text.

لگانے سے بیع فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی ۔ اور امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ لوگوں کے تعامل کی وجہ سے استحسانا اس صورت میں بیع جائز ہے ۔ اس پر فتویٰ ہے۔ ہاں اگر پھلوں کی بڑھا ور پوری نہیں ہوئی بلکہ ان کے حجم میں اضافہ متوقع ہے تو شرط ترک کے ساتھ بالا تفاق بیع جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں جزء معدوم کی شرط ہے اور یہ وہ جز ہے جو زمین یا درخت کی قوت سے پیدا ہوگا اور یہ " جز عقد بیع کے بعد بالع کی ملک سے پیدا ہوا ہے تو گویا مشترکی نے موجود اور معدوم کو ملا کر خریدا ہے۔ اور معدوم اور موجود کو ملا کر خریدنے سے بیع فاسد ہوتی ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں بیع فاسد ہو گی ۔
From the condition, the sale becomes fasid. Therefore in this case the sale will be fasid. And Imam Muhammad said that due to people's practice, by istihsan, the sale is valid in this case. The fatwa is upon this. However, if the fruit's growth is not complete but an increase in volume is expected, then with the condition of leaving, by consensus the sale is not valid. Because in this case it is a condition of a non-existent part, and that part is that which is generated by the strength of the land or tree, and it is generated after the contract from the seller's property, so the buyer has bought the existing and non-existent together. And buying the non-existent and existing together makes the sale fasid. Therefore in this case the sale will be fasid.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of selling fruit with a condition that it remains on the tree. The base ruling states that such a condition renders the sale fasid (defective) because it involves a non-existent part (juz' ma'dum) that will come into existence from the seller's property after the contract. However, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, using istihsan (juristic preference) based on the customary practice of the people (ta'amul), considers the sale valid when the fruit's growth is complete. The text indicates that the fatwa is on Imam Muhammad's view. But if the fruit's growth is incomplete and an increase is expected, then even Imam Muhammad agrees the sale is invalid due to consensus, because the condition concerns a truly non-existent part. The reasoning is that buying something that partly exists and partly does not is like selling a future thing, which makes the contract fasid. The practical difference is that if the condition is attached and growth is complete, the sale is valid; otherwise it is not.

Key Terms
بیع فاسد (bay' fasid): A sale that is defective in a condition but can be rectified; here it means invalid due to the condition of a non-existent part.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that departs from strict analogy based on custom, necessity, or equity.
جزء معدوم (juz' ma'dum): A non-existent part; here refers to future increase in fruit that does not exist at the time of sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the mufta bihi ruling on selling fruit with a condition to leave it on the tree when the fruit's growth is complete?
A) The sale is fasid.
B) The sale is valid (jayiz).
C) The sale is batil.
D) The ruling depends on the price.

Key Takeaway
When selling fruit with a condition to leave it on the tree, the sale is valid (mufta bihi) if the fruit's growth is complete, based on custom and istihsan; otherwise, it is invalid by consensus.

Ruling on Increase of Fruit Left on Tree with and Without Permission
Ruling on increase of fruit left with/without permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the increase of fruit left on the tree after sale and apply the distinction between substantive increase and change of condition.

Core Idea
Increase without seller's permission is prohibited gain; after full growth, no substantive increase, so no charity.

This lesson from al-Hidayah examines a buyer who purchases fruit on the tree 'absolutely' (mutlaqan), meaning no condition on when to pick. The fruit may increase in substance (size, sweetness) while still on the tree. The key legal question: does the buyer own this increase? The answer hinges on whether the seller permitted the fruit to remain. If permission was given, the increase is halal. If not, the increase is considered obtained through a prohibited means (usurping benefit from the seller's property), so the buyer must give it in charity. However, if the fruit has already reached its full growth, any change (ripening, coloring) is not a substantive increase but a mere change of condition, and no charity is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main scenarios
The passage covers leaving fruit with seller's permission and without permission. Also a sub-scenario: after full growth.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
With permission: increase is halal. Without permission before full growth: must give increase in charity. Without permission after full growth: no charity.
3
Understand the reasoning (illah)
The illah for charity is that the increase was obtained through a prohibited means (jihah mahzurah) because the buyer benefited from the seller's property without consent. After full growth, no substantive increase occurs, only change of condition, so the illah is absent.
4
Distinguish between substantive increase and change of condition
Substantive increase (ziyadah fi al-dhat) is an actual addition to the fruit's substance, like growth in size or weight. Change of condition (taghayyur hal) is a transformation like ripening or coloring, which involves no new matter from the seller's property.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical case
If a buyer buys dates on a tree and leaves them without permission, and the dates become sweeter and larger, he must give the extra weight in charity. But if they were already full-sized and just ripened, no charity needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اشتراها مطلقا وتركها باذن البائع طاب له الفضل وان تركها بغير اذنه تصدق بما زاد في ذاته لحصوله بجهة محظورة وان تركها بعد ماتنا هي عظمها لم يتصدق بشئى لان هذا تغير حالة لاتحقق زيادة .
And if he bought them absolutely and left them with the permission of the seller, the increase is permissible for him. And if he left them without his permission, he gives in charity what increased in its substance because it was obtained by a prohibited means. And if he left them after they attained their full growth, he gives nothing in charity because this is a change of condition, not a verification of increase.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof on the increase of fruit when a buyer purchases fruit absolutely (without any condition) and leaves them on the tree. There are two scenarios: with the seller's permission and without. With permission, any increase in the fruit's substance (like size or sweetness) during the period it remains on the tree is halal for the buyer, as the seller consented. Without permission, the buyer benefits from the seller's property (the tree and land) without right, which is akin to benefiting from usurped property. Therefore, the increase is obtained through a prohibited means, and it must be given in charity. However, if the fruit has already reached its full growth (tahiyy 'uthm), no further increase in substance occurs; only changes like ripening, coloring, and flavoring happen, which are not from the seller's property but from external factors (sun, moon, stars). Thus, no charity is required.

Key Terms
مطلقا (mutlaqan): Absolutely, without any condition attached to the sale.
فضل (fadl): Increase, especially in value or substance of the fruit.
جهة محظورة (jihah mahzurah): A prohibited means; here, benefiting without permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Keep the increase
B) Give the increase in charity
C) Return the fruit to the seller
D) Pay the seller for the increase

Key Takeaway
The increase of fruit left without permission must be given in charity if it is a substantive increase; after full growth, changes are not substantive, so no charity is required.

Batil vs Fasid Leases: When the Increase is Permissible
Ruling on increase in fruit vs crop leases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a batil and a fasid lease in Hanafi law and apply the correct ruling on the permissibility of increase in sale-and-leaseback scenarios.

Core Idea
A batil lease is legally non-existent so permission remains; a fasid lease corrupts permission.

In Hanafi fiqh, not all invalid contracts are treated equally. The difference between a void (batil) and a defective (fasid) contract can determine whether an increase in property is halal or tainted. This lesson examines a key ruling from Al-Hidayah on buying fruit while leasing the trees, contrasting it with the analogous case of crops and land.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two parallel cases: (1) buying fruit and leasing the trees until ripening, and (2) buying crops and leasing the land until ripening. Identify each act and the ruling on the increase.
2
Classify the lease types
For the fruit case, the tree lease is classified as batil (void) because there is no customary practice or need for such a lease. For the crop case, the land lease is fasid (defective) due to ignorance (jahalah) about the benefit. Understand why each lease type differs.
Batil is non-existent in essence and effect; fasid exists in essence but is defective.
3
Determine the legal consequence for the increase
Since a batil lease is considered non-existent, the seller's implicit permission for the fruit to remain remains effective, making the increase halal. For the fasid land lease, the defect taints the permission, making the increase not halal.
The result hinges on the contract's legal existence, not just its invalidity.
4
Analyze the underlying analogy (qiyas)
The ruling uses qiyas: both cases involve a sale of produce with a lease for ripening, but the nature of the lease (batil vs fasid) changes the outcome. The justification (illah) is that batil leases do not affect prior permissions, while fasid leases do.
This is a form of qiyas jaliyy based on contractual categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اشتراها مطلقا وتركها على النخيل وقداستاجر النخيل الى وقت الادراك طاب له الفضل لان الاجارة باطلة لعدم التعارف والحاجة فبقى الاذن معتبرا بخلاف ما اذا اشترى الزرع واستاجر الارض الى ان یدرک وتركه حيث لا يطيب له الفضل لان الاجارة فاسدة للجهالة فاورثت خبثا
And if he bought them absolutely and left them on the palm trees, and he had leased the palm trees until the time of ripening, the increase is permissible for him because the lease is batil due to lack of customary practice and need, so the permission remains effective. Unlike if he bought crops and leased the land until ripening and left them, where the increase is not permissible for him because the lease is fasid due to ignorance, so it causes impurity.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where a buyer purchases fruit absolutely and also leases the trees on which the fruit is growing until the fruit ripens. The ruling states that the increase during this period is halal for the buyer. The reasoning is that the lease of trees is batil (void) because there is no customary practice (ta'aruf) and no need for such a lease (since the buyer could have bought the fruit with the tree). A batil contract is considered non-existent, so it does not affect the permission that the seller implicitly gave by allowing the fruit to remain. Therefore, the increase is treated as if left with permission. In contrast, if someone buys crops and leases the land until ripening, the lease is fasid (defective) due to ignorance (jahalah) about the exact benefit, and this fasid contract causes impurity (khabath), making the increase not halal. A fasid contract is existent in essence but defective, so it taints the permission. The text also explains the difference between batil and fasid: batil is non-existent in both essence and description, while fasid exists in essence but is defective in description.

Key Terms
اجارة باطلة (ijarah batilah): A lease that is void ab initio, lacking essential elements or condition, considered non-existent.
اجارة فاسدة (ijarah fasidah): A lease that exists in essence but defective due to ignorance or other fault.
خبث (khabath): Impurity or unlawfulness; here, the fasid lease causes the increase to be tainted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the lease is valid and allows the fruit to stay
B) Because the lease is batil and therefore the seller's permission remains
C) Because the buyer owns the trees
D) Because the fruit is already ripe

Key Takeaway
The classification of an invalid contract as batil or fasid determines whether associated gains are permissible: batil does not taint, fasid does.

Leasing Trees After Buying Fruit: Batil vs Fasid
Rules on excess when leasing trees vs. land after buying produce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a batil (void) and a fasid (irregular) lease in the context of buying produce and determine the legal effect on excess growth.

Core Idea
A void lease (batil) leaves the seller's permission intact; an irregular lease (fasid) contaminates it — the distinction changes the ruling on excess.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a comparative ruling that tests the Hanafi contractual categories of batil (void) and fasid (irregular). By examining two scenarios — leasing trees after buying fruit versus leasing land after buying crops — we uncover how the nature of the defect (absence of custom and need vs. ignorance of duration) determines whether the increase is halal or impure. Understanding this distinction is key to applying the correct ruling in similar transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and isolate the first case (buying fruit, leasing trees) and the second case (buying crop, leasing land). Note the different rulings on excess growth.
The first case: excess halal. Second case: excess not halal.
2
Analyze the contractual classification
For each scenario, identify why the lease is classified as batil or fasid. The passage states that leasing trees is batil due to lack of custom and need, while leasing land is fasid due to ignorance of the exact duration.
Batil: legally non-existent. Fasid: exists in essence but defective in attribute.
3
Understand the legal mechanism
Trace how the classification affects the seller's permission: a batil lease cannot carry the permission, so the permission stands independently; a fasid lease implies the permission, making it also fasid and impure.
Objection and answer in the passage clarifies this.
4
Apply the ruling to similar cases
Consider other scenarios where a buyer leases an asset after buying its produce. Determine which classification applies and the ruling on excess.
Use the same reasoning based on custom, need, and clarity of duration.

ہوگی اور جب اجارہ فاسد ہے اور بائع کی اجازت بھی فاسد ہے تو کھیتی میں جو کچھ اضافہ ہوگا اس میں نجاست اور خبث پیدا ہوگا اور جس چیز میں خبث پیدا ہوتا ہے۔ وہ حلال نہیں ہوتی اس لئے یہ زیادتی مشتری کے لئے حلال نہ ہو گی۔
If he buys them absolutely and leaves them on the palm trees, and he has leased the palm trees until the time of ripening, the excess is permissible for him because the lease is void due to lack of custom and need, so the permission remains valid. Unlike if he buys the crop and leases the land until it ripens and leaves it; the excess is not permissible for him because the lease is irregular due to ignorance, so it causes impurity. Explanation: The difference between void and irregular is that void is non-existent legally, having no essence or attribute; irregular exists in essence but is non-existent in attribute. The case: If someone buys fruit on trees before the great limit (tanaahi azim) without condition, and leases the trees until ripening, any increase is halal for the buyer because the lease is void due to lack of custom and need. The permission of the seller remains. Objection: The permission is implied in the lease, and since the lease is void, the permission is also void, making the fruit left without permission, requiring charity. Answer: The void lease is legally non-existent and cannot imply anything; the permission stands independently. However, if someone buys crop and leases the land until ripening, the lease is irregular due to unknown duration, so the lease exists in essence and implies the permission, which then becomes irregular, causing impurity, hence the excess is not halal.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the chapter of sales, comparing two scenarios of buying produce and then leasing the underlying asset until ripening. The first case: a person buys fruit on trees absolutely (no condition to cut or leave) and leases the trees until the fruit ripens. The excess growth during this period is halal (permissible) for the buyer. The reason is that leasing trees for this purpose is not customary and there is no real need (since the buyer could purchase the trees along with the fruit). Therefore the lease is batil (void) – legally non-existent. Since a void contract cannot carry any legal effect, the seller's permission for the buyer to leave the fruit on the trees remains valid and independent. Consequently, the increase in the fruit is considered as growing on the buyer's own property. The second case: a person buys a crop (standing grain) and leases the land until the crop ripens. Here the excess is not halal for the buyer because the lease of land is fasid (irregular) due to ignorance of the exact duration (ripening time depends on weather). A fasid contract exists in its essence (unlike batil) and therefore can include permission. That permission becomes fasid as well, imparting impurity (khabath) to the increase, making it unlawful. The passage also explains the difference between batil (void) and fasid (irregular). This ruling is based on rational reasoning (istihsan) considering custom and necessity.

Key Terms
باطل (batil): A contract that is void in its essence and attribute; legally non-existent.
فاسد (fasid): A contract that exists in its essence but is defective in attribute (e.g., due to uncertainty); requires rectification.
اجارہ (ijarah): A lease contract for the use of an asset for a specified period in exchange for rent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first scenario (buying fruit and leasing trees), why is the excess (increase in fruit) halal for the buyer?
A) Because the lease of trees is valid and the increase is included
B) Because the lease is batil (void) so the seller's permission stands, and the increase is on the buyer's property
C) Because the buyer owns the trees, so any increase is automatically his
D) Because the lease is fasid (irregular) but the increase is permitted by custom

Key Takeaway
The distinction between batil (void) and fasid (irregular) contracts determines whether the seller's permission survives and whether excess growth is halal or impure.

Ruling on New Fruit Appearing Before or After Possession
Ruling with rational proof on fruit sale and new growth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when new fruit appears on trees before and after possession, and explain the rationale based on delivery impossibility and mixture.

Core Idea
Sale of fruit is fasid if new fruit appears before possession; after possession it is valid but parties become co-owners.

This lesson deals with a common scenario in agricultural sales: when fruit on trees is sold without condition, and new fruit grows before or after the buyer takes possession. The ruling hinges on whether the seller can still deliver the exact sold item. We will explore the reasoning and the practical solution offered by Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sale subject
The fruit is sold absolutely (mutilaq) – no condition to cut or leave. The sold fruit is on the trees at the time of contract.
Absolute sale means the buyer has the right to take possession immediately.
2
Determine timing of new fruit
New fruit may appear either before the buyer takes possession (qabd) or after. This timing determines the ruling.
Qabd is the transfer of physical control.
3
Apply the ruling for each case
If new fruit appears before possession, the sale is fasid because the seller cannot deliver the exact sold fruit – sold and unsold are mixed indistinguishably. If after possession, the sale remains valid, but the new fruit (seller's property) mixes with the sold fruit, creating co-ownership.
The buyer's word is accepted on the quantity of new fruit because he is the possessor.
4
Note the practical solution
To avoid co-ownership and potential disputes, the buyer can purchase the trees themselves (usul). Then any new growth belongs to the buyer as it arises on his property.
This is called al-mukhlis (the legal escape).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مطلقاً پھل خریدے پھر قبل القبض یا بعد القبض دوسرے پھل بھی ان میں پیدا ہو گئے تو بیع کا حکم

ولو اشتراها مطلقا فاثمرت ثمرا اخر قبل القبض فسد البيع لانه لا يمكنه تسليم المبيع لتعذرا التمييز ولو اثمرت بعد القبض يشتركان فيه للاختلاط والقول قول المشترى فى مقداره لانه فى يده وكذافي الباذنجان والبطيخ والمخلص ان يشترى الاصول ليحصل الزيادة على ملكه

ترجمہ: اور اگر اس نے پھلوں کو مطلقاً خریدا پھر قبضہ سے پہلے دوسرے پھل آگئے تو بیع فاسد ہوگئی ۔ کیونکہ بائع کے لئے مبیع سپرد کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ ( صبیح اور غیر بیج کے درمیان ) امتیاز کرنا محال ہے۔ اور اگر قبضہ کے بعد ( نئے ) پھل آئے تو بائع اور مشتری ان میں دونوں شریک ہو جائیں گے ۔ کیونکہ ( مبیع اور غیر مبیع مختلط ہوگئی ہے۔ اور زائد پھلوں کی مقدار میں مشتری کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ پھل اس کے قبضہ میں ہیں۔ اور یہی حکم بینگن اور خربوزہ میں ہے۔ اور چھٹکارے کی صورت یہ ہے کہ درختوں کو خرید لے تا کہ زیادتی مشتری کی ملک پر حاصل ہو۔

تشریح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے درخت پر لگے ہوئے پھل خریدے اور انکو توڑنے یا چھوڑنے کی کوئی شرط نہیں کی بلکہ ان کو یونہی چھوڑے رکھا پس اس درمیان میں کچھ نئے پھل انھیں درختوں پر پیدا ہو گئے تو اگر یہ نئے پھل مشتری کے قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے پیدا ہو گئے تو بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ جو پھل مبیع ہیں اور جو پھل نئے پیدا ہوئے ہیں ان میں امتیاز کرنا چونکہ محال ہے اس لئے بائع کے واسطے مبیع سپرد کرنا ناممکن ہو گیا۔ اور جس صورت میں بیع سپرد کرنا متعذر اور ناممکن ہو اس صورت میں بیع فاسد ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے قبضہ سے پہلے نئے پھل پیدا ہونے کی صورت میں بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ اور اگر مشتری کے قبضہ کرنے کے بعد نئے پھل پیدا ہوئے ہوں تو بیع فاسد نہ ہوگی کیونکہ مبیع سپرد کر دی گئی ہے۔ البتہ بائع کی ملک یعنی وہ پھل جو قبضہ کرنے کے بعد پیدا ہوئے ہیں مشتری کی ملک یعنی ان پھلوں کے ساتھ مل گئے ہیں جو مشتری نے خریدے ہیں اور اختلاط بھی ایسا ہو گیا کہ دونوں میں امتیاز کرنا محال ہے۔ اس لئے بائع اور مشتری دونوں ان پھلوں میں شریک ہونگے اور جو پھل نئے پیدا ہوئے ہیں ان کی مقدار بیان کرنے میں مشتری کا قول معتبر ہوگا۔ کیونکہ نئے پرانے تمام پھل مشتری کے قبضہ میں ہیں اور مقدار مقبوض کے سلسلہ میں قابض ہی کا قول معتبر ہوگا ہے ۔ اس لئے یہاں بھی قابض یعنی مشتری کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ یہی حکم بینگن اور خربوزہ اور دوسرے پھلوں کا ہے۔ یعنی اگر کسی نے بینگن یا خربوزے یا دوسرے پھل خریدے اور پھر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے نئے بینگن یا خربوزے پیدا ہو گئے تو بیع فاسد ہو جائے گی اور اگر قبضہ کے بعد پیدا ہوئے تو بائع اور مشتری دونوں شریک ہو جائیں گے۔
If he buys them absolutely and then another fruit appears before possession, the sale becomes fasid because delivery is impossible due to inability to distinguish. If they appear after possession, they share them due to mixture, and the buyer's word is taken regarding the quantity because they are in his hand. Similarly for eggplant and melon. The solution is to buy the roots (trees) so that the increase occurs on his property. Translation: If he buys the fruit absolutely and then other fruit appears before possession, the sale is fasid because the seller cannot deliver the sold item as distinguishing between sold and unsold is impossible. If they appear after possession, the seller and buyer become partners in them due to mixture. The buyer's word is taken regarding the new fruit's quantity because they are in his possession. The same ruling applies to eggplant and melon. The solution is to buy the trees so that the increase occurs on his property. Explanation: The case is a person buys fruit on trees without condition. Then new fruit appears. If before possession, the sale is fasid because the sold and unsold are indistinguishable, making delivery impossible. If after possession, the sale remains valid but the new fruit (seller's property) mixes with the sold fruit (buyer's property). Since they are inseparable, they become partners. The buyer's word is believed regarding the quantity of new fruit because he is the possessor. Same for eggplant, melon, and similar produce.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage from the chapter of sales deals with a problem when fruit on trees is bought absolutely (without a condition to cut or leave) and new fruit grows on the same trees before or after the buyer takes possession. The ruling distinguishes two scenarios: (1) If new fruit appears before the buyer takes possession (qabd), the sale becomes fasid (irregular) because the seller cannot deliver the exact sold item—the sold and unsold fruit are mixed indistinguishably. A fundamental condition of sale is the ability to deliver the subject matter, so the contract is defective. (2) If new fruit appears after the buyer has taken possession, the sale remains valid because delivery of the original sold fruit has already occurred. However, the new fruit (still owned by the seller) becomes mixed with the sold fruit in the buyer's hands inseparably. Consequently, the seller and buyer become co-owners (sharika) in the mixed fruit proportionally. Since the buyer is the possessor, his statement about the quantity of the new fruit is accepted (with oath if needed), as the general principle is that the possessor's word is taken regarding the amount in his possession. The same ruling applies to other produce like eggplant and melon that grow multiple times or continuously. A practical solution to avoid this complication is for the buyer to purchase the trees (the roots/plants) themselves, so that any future growth occurs on his own property and no mixing of ownership occurs.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Taking possession or physical control of the sold item.
اختلاط (ikhtilat): Mixture or intermingling of two properties such that they are indistinguishable.
مخلص (mukhlis): A solution or way out of a legal difficulty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If new fruit appears before possession, why is the sale fasid?
A) Because the fruit is not ownable
B) Because the seller cannot deliver the exact sold fruit due to indistinguishability
C) Because the price was unknown
D) Because the buyer did not see the fruit

Key Takeaway
The key in fruit sales is the ability to deliver the exact sold items; if new growth makes separation impossible before possession, the sale is defective, but after possession it creates co-ownership.

Ruling on Excepting Known Pounds When Selling Fruit
Ruling on excepting known pounds from fruit sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi ruling on excepting known pounds from a fruit sale, EXPLAIN the Hanafi dalil of jahalah, and EVALUATE the Maliki qiyas argument.

Core Idea
A sale becomes fasid if the remainder after exception is unknown, even if the excepted amount is specified.

This passage deals with a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Maliki schools regarding a sale of fruit on trees where the seller excludes a known weight (e.g., 100 pounds). The Hanafi school, as articulated by al-Quduri, deems such a sale invalid because the remaining quantity becomes unknown, leading to potential dispute. Imam Malik, however, permits it by analogy to excepting specific trees. The text also reveals an internal Hanafi difference between the relied-upon transmission (zahir al-riwayah) and a weaker narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad and al-Tahawi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What exactly is being disputed? It is the validity of selling fruit on trees while excepting a known weight (e.g., 100 pounds). Determine the subject and the exception.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school holds that such a sale is fasid (void) because the remainder after exception is majhul (unknown) in quality and quantity. This ignorance (jahl) leads to dispute and is prohibited.
Also consider the exceptional case where the excepted amount might equal the total fruit, making the sold item nonexistent.
3
Analyze the Maliki counter-argument
Imam Malik argues by qiyas: just as selling a garden and excepting specific trees is permissible (because the remainder is known by sight), so too should excepting known pounds be permissible. Identify the analogy and test it.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafis rebut the qiyas: in the tree exception, the remainder is known through direct visual observation (mushahada), whereas after excepting pounds, the fruit's quality and exact remaining quantity are unknown. The analogy fails due to this difference in certainty.
Also, the text notes a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad that opposes the majority Hanafi view, but the mufta bihi is the majority.
5
Determine the practical outcome
The thamarah al-khilaf: in the Hanafi school, the contract is fasid and must be rescinded; in the Maliki school, it is valid. Understand the consequence for a real-world transaction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پھلوں کی معین مقدار مستثنیٰ کرنے کا حکم قال ولا يجوزان يبيع ثمرة ويستثنى منها ارطالا معلومة خلا فالمالك لان الباقي بعد الاستثناء مجهول بخلاف ما اذا باع واستثنى نخلا معينا لان الباقى معلوم بالمشاهدة قال قالواهذا رواية الحسن وهو قول الطحاوى اما على ظاهر الرواية ينبغى ان يجوز لان الاصل ان ما يجوز ايراد العقد عليه بانفراده يجور استثناؤه من العقد وبيع قفيز من صبرة جائز فكذا استثناؤه بخلاف استثنا الحمل واطراف الحيوان لانه لا يجوز بيعه فكذا استثناؤه ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ پھلوں کو بیچنا اور ان میں سے ارطال معلومہ کا استثناء کرنا جائز نہیں ہے امام مالک کا اختلاف ہے ۔ کیونکہ استثناء کے بعد جو کچھ باقی رہا وہ مجہول ہے۔ برخلاف اس کے کہ اگر باغ بیچا اور ایک معین درخت کا استثناء کیا کیونکہ جو باقی ہے وہ مشاہدہ سے معلوم ہے۔ مصنف ہدایہ نے کہا کہ مشائخ نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ حسن کی روایت ہے۔ اور یہی طحاوی کا قول ہے۔ بہر حال ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق جائز ہونا چاہئے۔ اس لئے کہ ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ جس چیز سے تنہا عقد کرنا جائز ہے اس کا عقد سے استثناء بھی جائز ہے۔ اور اناج کے ڈھیر سے ایک قفیز کی بیع جائز ہے تو اس کا استثناء بھی جائز ہے۔ برخلاف حمل اور اطراف حیوان کے استثناء کے کہ ان کو تنہا بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ لہذا ان کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ درختوں پر لگے ہوئے پھلوں کا بیچنا اور چند متعین ارطال کو مستثنی کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مثلا یہ کہے کہ میں نے اس باغ کے پھل فروخت کئے سوائے ایک مونا کے یا اس باغ کے آم فروخت کئے سوائے ایک ہزار آم کے تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور حضرت امام مالک کے نزدیک جائز ہے ۔ امام مالک کی دلیل قیاس ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح باغ بیچنا اور متعین درختوں کا استثناء کرنا جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح ارطال معلومہ کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ احناف کی دلیل ... ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ارطال معلومہ کا استثناء کرنے کے بعد جو مقدار باقی رہتی ہے وہ مجہول ہے۔ بایں طور کہ بائع مطالبہ کرے گا جنس میں عمدہ پھلوں کا اور مشتری اس کو گھٹیا پھل دیگا تو یہ جہالت مفضی الی المنازعہ ہوگی۔ اور ایسی جہالت کے ہوتے ہوئے بیع جائز نہیں ہوتی۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اس کے علاوہ ایک خرابی یہ بھی ہے کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ باغ میں کل پھل اتنے ہی ہوں جس قدر کہ مستی ہیں۔ پس اس صورت میں مبیع ہی معدوم ہو جائے گی۔ اور مبیع معدوم ہونے کی صورت میں بھی بیع جائز نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ ہاں اگر باغ بیچا اور چند معین درختوں کا استثناء کیا تو استثناء کے بعد جو درخت باقی رہ گئے چونکہ وہ مشاہدہ سے معلوم ہیں اس لئے اس صورت میں بیج جائز ہے۔
Ruling on excepting a specified quantity of fruit: He (al-Quduri) said: It is not permissible to sell fruit and except from it known pounds, unlike Imam Malik. Because what remains after the exception is unknown, contrary to when one sells and excepts a specific palm tree, because what remains is known by sight. He (the author of Hidayah) said: The scholars said this is the narration of Hasan and the saying of al-Tahawi. But according to zahir al-riwayah, it should be permissible because the principle is that whatever is permissible to contract upon individually, its exception from a contract is permissible. And selling a qafiz from a heap is permissible, so likewise is excepting it. Contrary to excepting a pregnancy or the limbs of an animal, because selling them alone is not permissible, so excepting them is also not permissible. Translation: Al-Quduri said that selling fruits and excepting known pounds from them is not permissible, and Imam Malik disagrees. Because after the exception, what remains is unknown. Unlike if he sold the garden and excepted a specific tree, because what remains is known by sight. The author of Hidayah said that the scholars said this is the narration of Hasan and the saying of al-Tahawi. However, according to zahir al-riwayah, it should be permissible because the principle is that whatever can be contracted upon individually can be excepted from a contract. And selling a qafiz from a heap is permissible, so its exception is also permissible. Contrary to excepting a pregnancy or the limbs of an animal, because selling them alone is not permissible, so their exception is also not permissible. Explanation: The scenario is that selling fruits on trees and excepting a few specified pounds is not permissible. For example, he says, 'I have sold the fruits of this garden except one maund' or 'I have sold the mangoes of this garden except one thousand mangoes' – this is not permissible. According to Imam Malik, it is permissible. Imam Malik's proof is qiyas: just as selling a garden and excepting specific trees is permissible, likewise excepting known pounds is permissible. The Hanafi proof... Our proof is that after excepting known pounds, the remaining quantity is unknown. That is, the seller will demand good quality fruits and the buyer will give bad ones, so this ignorance leads to dispute. And such ignorance makes the sale invalid. Also another problem: it is possible that the total fruits in the garden are exactly the amount excepted, so the sold item would be nonexistent. And a sale with a nonexistent item is not permissible. Yes, if one sells the garden and excepts a few specific trees, then the remaining trees (after exception) are known by sight, so the sale is permissible.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafis and Imam Malik, with an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf. The issue: selling fruit on trees and excepting a known quantity (like 100 pounds) from the sale. Al-Quduri rules it invalid because the remainder becomes unknown (majhul), leading to dispute. Imam Malik says it is permissible by qiyas to excepting specific trees. The Hanafi response: the remainder is unknown, leading to potential conflict, and also the possibility that the excepted amount equals the total fruit, making the sold item nonexistent. The text also notes an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf: according to a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad and al-Tahawi, it is invalid, but according to zahir al-riwayah (the relied-upon transmission), it should be permissible because the principle is that anything that can be sold individually can be excepted from a larger contract. The author of Hidayah inclines towards permissibility based on the principle. However, the standard Hanafi position as per the commentary is that it is not permissible due to ignorance. The passage concludes by affirming that excepting specific trees is valid because the remainder is known by sight.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna'): A legal exception in a sale contract, where the seller excludes certain items from the sale.
ارطال معلومة (artal ma'luma): Known pounds or specified weight; a well-defined quantity by weight.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The authoritative transmission of the Hanafi school, primarily from the six books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), what is the ruling on selling fruit on trees and excepting a known weight (e.g., 100 pounds)?
A) Valid, because the excepted amount is known.
B) Invalid, because the remainder after exception is unknown.
C) Valid, following Imam Malik.
D) Invalid only if the excepted amount exceeds half the fruit.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi sales law, an istithna' that leaves the remainder unknown renders the contract fasid, even if the excepted quantity is precisely specified.

Hila to Save Fruit Sale When New Fruit Appears Before Possession
Describes a legal trick to avoid invalidation of a fruit sale due to new fruit growth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hila for avoiding invalidation of a fruit sale when new fruit appears before possession and identify the condition on which it depends.

Core Idea
Buying the trees along with the fruit transfers ownership of new fruit, salvaging an otherwise invalid sale.

In Hanafi fiqh, a fruit sale can become invalid if new fruit appears after the contract but before the buyer takes possession. This lesson presents a legal stratagem (hila) from al-Hidayah to rescue such a sale. The key is to restructure the transaction: the buyer purchases the trees as well, making them the owner of any new fruit. After harvest, the trees are sold back to the original seller at cost – but only if the seller trusts the buyer to fulfill the repurchase.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
The sale of fruit on trees becomes fasid (voidable) if new fruit appears before the buyer takes possession. This is because the new fruit is not included in the original contract, leading to uncertainty (gharar) or potential riba.
The default Hanafi rule: ownership is transferred upon contract, but risk and newly arising produce remain with the seller until possession.
2
Restructure the Transaction
The hila: the buyer increases the price slightly and also buys the trees. Now the buyer owns both the existing fruit and the trees. Any new fruit that appears is automatically owned by the buyer.
By purchasing the trees, the buyer gains ownership of the trees themselves, so any new growth belongs to the buyer.
3
Understand the Effect
Because the buyer owns the trees, the new fruit belongs to the buyer. The original sale becomes valid (ja'iz) because the uncertainty is eliminated.
This is a transaction not a separate sale of future fruit; it is a sale of the trees with fruit included.
4
Post-Harvest Repurchase
After the buyer picks the fruit, the buyer sells the trees back to the seller at exactly the same price paid for them (the cost).
The trees are returned to the seller at cost, no profit is intended on the trees themselves.
5
Identify the Trust Condition
This hila only works if the seller is confident that the buyer will indeed sell the trees back at the agreed price. If trust is lacking, the hila cannot be used.
The trust condition is crucial: the seller must have assurance from the buyer regarding the repurchase.

Source Text

صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قبضہ سے پہلے نئے پھل پیدا ہونے کی صورت میں فساد بیج سے چھٹکارے کی شکل یہ ہے کہ مشتری پھلوں کے ساتھ کچھ دام بڑھا کر درختوں کو بھی خرید لے ۔ اب جو بھی نئے پھل آئیں گے وہ سب مشتری کی ملک میں آئیں گے۔ اور سب کا مالک مشتری ہوگا۔ اور بیع جائز ہو جائے گی ۔ پھر پھل توڑنے کے بعد درخت اسی قیمت پر جس قیمت پر خریدے ہیں، بائع کے ہاتھ فروخت کر دے۔ لیکن یہ جب ہی ممکن ہے جبکہ بائع کو مشتری کی طرف سے اطمینان ہو کہ وہ مجھے اسی قیمت پر واپس کر دے گا۔
The author of Hidaya says: In the case where new fruit appears before possession, the way to escape from the invalid sale is that the buyer increases the price slightly and also buys the trees. Now, whatever new fruit appears will all come into the ownership of the buyer. And the buyer will be the owner of all. And the sale will become valid. Then, after picking the fruit, the buyer sells the trees back to the seller at the same price at which he bought them. But this is only possible if the seller is confident from the buyer that he will return the trees at that price.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents a specific legal remedy (hila) within the Hanafi madhhab for a sale that would otherwise become invalid due to new fruit appearing after the contract but before possession. The problem arises because, according to Hanafi fiqh, if fruit appears after a sale of fruit on trees, the original sale may be tainted with riba or gharar. The solution is to restructure the transaction: the buyer purchases both the existing fruit and the trees (at an increased price), thus owning all future fruit. After the harvest, the buyer sells the trees back to the seller at cost. This trick only works if the seller trusts the buyer to fulfill the repurchase. The passage type is a ruling statement providing a practical exit from a prohibited situation.

Key Terms
قبضہ (qabḍah): Possession or taking delivery of the purchased item.
فساد بیج (fasād bay‘): An invalid or corrupted sale due to a defect in contract.
حیلہ (hīlah): A legal stratagem to achieve a permitted outcome while avoiding prohibition.

Key Takeaway
The hila to avoid invalidation of a fruit sale due to new fruit before possession is to purchase the trees along with the fruit and then sell them back after harvest, but only works when the seller trusts the buyer to repurchase.

Selling Fruit with Exception of Known Pounds: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on excluding known pounds from fruit sale with internal Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on selling fruit with exception of known pounds and state the muftā bihī position with its underlying principle.

Core Idea
Whatever can be sold alone can be excepted—even in fruit sales with known weight.

This lesson examines a classical Hanafi dispute about selling fruit while excluding a specified weight (like pounds). The initial ruling in al-Quduri's matn prohibits it, but the commentary in al-Hidayah clarifies that the relied-upon position (zāhir al-riwāyah) allows it. You will learn the principle that governs exceptions in sales and why the Hanafi school ultimately permits this transaction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
Determine what exactly is being disputed: selling fruit with an exception of a known weight (e.g., pounds).
The object is fruit on trees, and the exception is a specific quantity like 'one maun' or 'one thousand mangoes'.
2
State the initial ruling and its source
Al-Quduri states the sale is not permissible. Note that this is a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad and also the view of Imam al-Tahawi.
This is a minority narration within the Hanafi school.
3
Explain the zāhir al-riwāyah position
The manifest narration (zāhir al-riwāyah) holds it permissible, based on the principle: whatever can be sold alone can be excepted. Selling a qafiz from a heap is permissible, so excepting it is permissible.
This is the muftā bihī (operative) position.
4
Address the objections and responses
Understand two objections: (1) the remaining fruit is unknown, (2) the exception may equal the whole. The responses: (1) fruit sales are by estimation, so sight suffices; (2) exception of the whole from itself is void, leaving a valid sale of all fruit.
These objections are raised by the opposing view (Malik, Shafi‘i, Ahmad) and the minority Hanafi narration.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis following zāhir al-riwāyah may execute such sales; Shafi‘is and Malikis prohibit them.
This shows how a difference in usul (principle) leads to different rulings in practice.

Source Text

پھلوں کی معین مقدار مستثنیٰ کرنے کا حکم
قال ولا يجوزان يبيع ثمرة ويستثنى منها ارطالا معلومة خلا فالمالك لان الباقي بعد الاستثناء مجهول بخلاف ما اذا باع واستثنى نخلا معينا لان الباقى معلوم بالمشاهدة قال قالواهذا رواية الحسن وهو قول الطحاوى اما على ظاهر الرواية ينبغى ان يجوز لان الاصل ان ما يجوز ايراد العقد عليه بانفراده يجور استثناؤه من العقد وبيع قفيز من صبرة جائز فكذا استثناؤه بخلاف استثنا الحمل واطراف الحيوان لانه لا يجوز بيعه فكذا استثناؤه
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ پھلوں کو بیچنا اور ان میں سے ارطال معلومہ کا استثناء کرنا جائز نہیں ہے امام مالک کا اختلاف ہے ۔ کیونکہ استثناء کے بعد جو کچھ باقی رہا وہ مجہول ہے۔ برخلاف اس کے کہ اگر باغ بیچا اور ایک معین درخت کا استثناء کیا کیونکہ جو باقی ہے وہ مشاہدہ سے معلوم ہے۔ مصنف ہدایہ نے کہا کہ مشائخ نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ حسن کی روایت ہے۔ اور یہی طحاوی کا قول ہے۔ بہر حال ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق جائز ہونا چاہئے۔ اس لئے کہ ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ جس چیز سے تنہا عقد کرنا جائز ہے اس کا عقد سے استثناء بھی جائز ہے۔ اور اناج کے ڈھیر سے ایک قفیز کی بیع جائز ہے تو اس کا استثناء بھی جائز ہے۔ برخلاف حمل اور اطراف حیوان کے استثناء کے کہ ان کو تنہا بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ لہذا ان کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ درختوں پر لگے ہوئے پھلوں کا بیچنا اور چند متعین ارطال کو مستثنی کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مثلا یہ کہے کہ میں نے اس باغ کے پھل فروخت کئے سوائے ایک مونا کے یا اس باغ کے آم فروخت کئے سوائے ایک ہزار آم کے تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور حضرت امام مالک کے نزدیک جائز ہے ۔ امام مالک کی دلیل قیاس ہے۔ یعنی جس طرح باغ بیچنا اور متعین درختوں کا استثناء کرنا جائز ہے۔ اسی طرح ارطال معلومہ کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ احناف کی دلیل ... ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ارطال معلومہ کا استثناء کرنے کے بعد جو مقدار باقی رہتی ہے وہ مجہول ہے۔ بایں طور کہ بائع مطالبہ کرے گا جنس میں عمدہ پھلوں کا اور مشتری اس کو گھٹیا پھل دیگا تو یہ جہالت مفضی الی المنازعہ ہوگی۔ اور ایسی جہالت کے ہوتے ہوئے بیع جائز نہیں ہوتی۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔ اس کے علاوہ ایک خرابی یہ بھی ہے کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ باغ میں کل پھل اتنے ہی ہوں جس قدر کہ مستی ہیں۔ پس اس صورت میں مبیع ہی معدوم ہو جائے گی۔ اور مبیع معدوم ہونے کی صورت میں بھی بیع جائز نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ ہاں اگر باغ بیچا اور چند معین درختوں کا استثناء کیا تو استثناء کے بعد جو درخت باقی رہ گئے چونکہ وہ مشاہدہ سے معلوم ہیں اس لئے اس صورت میں بیج جائز ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مشائخ نے فرمایا ہے کہ درختوں پر پھلوں کے بیچنے اور ار طال معلومہ کا استثناء کرنے کی صورت میں بیع کا عدم جواز امام ابو حنیفہ سے حسن بن زیاد کی روایت ہے۔ اور یہی امام طحاوی کا قول ہے۔ اور امام شافعی اور امام احمد بھی اسی کے قاتل ہیں۔ اور رہا ظاہر الروایہ کا حکم تو اس کے مطابق ارطال معلومہ کا استثناء کرنے کی صورت میں بھی جائز ہونی چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ ظاہر الروایہ میں یہ ضابطہ ذکر کیا گیا ہے کہ جس چیز کو تنہا فروخت کرنا جائز ہے اس کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ اور جس کو تنہا بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے اس کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً اناج کے ڈھیر میں سے ایک قفیز کی بیع جائز ہے تو پورے ڈھیر کو بیچنا اور ایک قفیز کو مستی کرنا بھی جائز ہے ۔ اور چونکہ فقط حمل کو بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ مثلا یوں کہے کہ میں نے اس بکری کو فروخت کیا نہ کہ اس کے حمل کو اور اسی طرح چونکہ حیوان کے تنہا عضو کو بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ مثلاً یوں کہے کہ میں نے اس بکری کو بیچا لیکن اس کی کھال کو نہیں بیچا۔ پس اس طرح چونکہ باغ کے پھلوں میں سے ارطال معلومہ کا تنہا بیچنا جائز ہے تو ارطال معلومہ کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ اور رہا یہ کہنا کہ مقدار مستثنیٰ کے بعد جو پھیل باقی ہیں وہ مجہول ہیں۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ بلاشبہ مجہول ہیں لیکن وزن کے اعتبار سے مجہول ہیں۔ مشاہدہ کے اعتبار سے مجہول نہیں ہیں۔ اور یہاں پھلوں کی بیع اندازہ سے کی گئی ہے نہ کہ وزن سے اور بیچ جب اندازہ سے کی جاتی ہے تو سبیع کا وزن یا کیل کے اعتبار سے معلوم ہونا ضروری نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اشارہ اور مشاہدہ سے معلوم ہونا کافی ہوتا ہے اور سیہ بات یہاں موجود ہے۔ اسلئے ارطال معلومہ کا استثناء کرنے کے باوجود بیچ درست ہوگی۔ اور رہا یہ کہنا کہ بسا اوقات پھلی اس قدر ہوتے ہیں جس قدر کا استثناء کیا گیا ہے تو مبیع ہی معدوم ہو جائے گی۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں گل کا استثناء گل سے ہوگا۔ اور گل کا استثنا محل سے باطل ہوتا ہے پس جب استثناء باطل ہوگیا تو بلا استثناء تمام پھلوں کی بیچ ہوئی۔ اور بلا استثناء باغ کے تمام پھلوں کی بیع جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی بیع جائز ہوگی۔
The Ruling on Excluding a Specific Quantity of Fruit
He (al-Quduri) said: It is not permissible to sell fruit and exclude from it known pounds, contrary to Malik, because the remainder after the exception is unknown. This is different from when one sells and excludes a specific palm tree, because the remainder is known by sight. He (the author of Hidaya) said: The scholars said this is the narration of Hasan (ibn Ziyad) and it is the saying of al-Tahawi. But according to the manifest narration (zahir al-riwayah), it should be permissible, because the principle is that whatever it is permissible to contract upon alone is permissible to exclude from the contract. Selling a qafiz from a heap is permissible, so similarly excluding it. This is unlike excepting an unborn animal or the limbs of an animal, because it is not permissible to sell them alone, so their exclusion is not permissible.
Translation: Quduri said: Selling fruit and excluding known pounds from it is not permissible; Imam Malik disagrees. Because after the exception, whatever remains is unknown. As opposed to if one sold a garden and excepted a specific tree, because what remains is known by sight. The author of Hidaya said that the scholars said this is the narration of Hasan (ibn Ziyad) and it is also the saying of Tahawi. Nevertheless, according to Zahir al-Riwayah, it should be permissible, because the rule is that whatever it is permissible to enter a contract upon alone, its exception from a contract is also permissible. And selling one qafiz from a heap is permissible, so its exception is also permissible. Contrary to excepting an unborn animal or the limbs of an animal, because it is not permissible to sell them alone, thus their exception is also not permissible.
Explanation: The case is that selling fruit on trees and excepting a few specific pounds is not permissible. For example, saying 'I sold the fruit of this garden except one maun' or 'I sold the mangoes of this garden except one thousand mangoes' - this is not permissible. And Imam Malik holds it permissible. Malik's proof is analogy: just as selling a garden and excepting specific trees is permissible, similarly excepting known pounds is permissible. Our proof (the Hanafi proof): After excepting known pounds, the remaining quantity is unknown, as the seller will demand good quality fruit and the buyer will give inferior fruit, leading to ignorance that leads to dispute. Such ignorance invalidates the sale. Additionally, there is the defect that it is possible the garden's total fruit equals exactly the excepted amount, in which case the sold object (mabī‘) becomes non-existent, also invalidating the sale. Yes, if one sells a garden and excepts specific trees, the remaining trees are known by sight, so the sale is permissible.
The author of Hidaya says: The scholars said that the impermissibility of selling fruit with exception of known pounds is a narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa, and it is also the saying of Tahawi. Imam Shafi‘i and Imam Ahmad also say this. But regarding the ruling of Zahir al-Riwayah, according to it, it should be permissible to except known pounds. Because in Zahir al-Riwayah, this principle is stated: Whatever it is permissible to sell alone, its exception is also permissible; and whatever it is not permissible to sell alone, its exception is also not permissible. For example, selling one qafiz from a heap of grain is permissible, so selling the entire heap and excepting one qafiz is also permissible. And since only the unborn animal is not permissible to sell, its exception is also not permissible. For example, saying 'I sold this goat but not its fetus'. Similarly, since it is not permissible to sell a limb of an animal alone, its exception is also not permissible. For example, saying 'I sold this goat but not its skin'. Thus, since it is permissible to sell known pounds from the garden's fruit alone, excepting known pounds is also permissible. As for the objection that after the exception the remaining fruit is unknown: We say, they are unknown by weight, but not unknown by sight. And the sale of fruit here is by estimation (khārzan), not by weight. When a sale is by estimation, it is not necessary that the weight or measure be known, but it is sufficient that it be known by indication and sight. That condition is present here. Therefore, the sale will be valid despite the exception of known pounds. As for the objection that sometimes the fruit is exactly the excepted amount, that would mean the sold object is non-existent: The answer is that in that case, the exception of the whole from the same kind (jins) is void, because the exception of the entire thing from itself is invalid. So when the exception becomes void, the sale of all fruit without exception remains. And the sale of all fruit of the garden without exception is valid. Hence, in this case too the sale is valid.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (and also includes an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Malik). The initial ruling from al-Quduri's matn states that selling fruit with an exception of a known weight (like pounds) is not permissible, and Imam Malik disagrees. The Hanafi grounds are that after the exception, the remaining fruit is unknown (majhūl), which leads to potential dispute. However, the commentary from the author of Hidaya clarifies that this ruling is based on a narration of Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa, but the relied-upon position (zāhir al-riwāyah) is that it is permissible. The principle is: whatever can be sold alone can be excepted. Since selling a known quantity from a heap is permissible, so is excepting it. The exception of an unborn animal or a limb is impermissible because they cannot be sold alone. The commentary then addresses two objections: (1) The remaining fruit is unknown by weight but known by sight, and since fruit sales are by estimation, this is acceptable. (2) If the entire fruit equals the exception, the exception is void (since it would be an exception of the whole from itself) and the sale stands for all fruit. Thus, the muftā bihī position in the Hanafi school is permissibility, in line with the zāhir al-riwāyah.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithnā'): The act of excluding a specific item or quantity from a sale contract.
ارطال (artāl): Plural of ratl, a unit of weight; here meaning 'pounds' or known weight units.
ظاہر الروایہ (Zāhir al-Riwāyah): The well-known transmitted rulings of the Hanafi school from Abu Hanifa and his main students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) in the six core books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the principle cited in the passage that allows the exception of known pounds from a fruit sale according to zāhir al-riwāyah?
A) The exception must be less than half the total fruit.
B) Whatever can be sold alone can be excepted from a sale.
C) The exception must be of a different type of fruit.
D) The exception must be specified by weight and measure.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi muftā bihī allows selling fruit with an exception of a known weight, based on the principle that what can be sold alone can be excepted, and the remaining fruit is sufficiently known by sight in estimation sales.
