Selling Grain in Spike and Pods: Hanafi Permissibility vs Shafi'i Prohibition
Ruling on selling wheat in spike and beans in pods, with Shafi'i objection based on covering.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling grain in spikes/pods, explain the Shafi'i objection, and apply the Hanafi hadith-based proof to refute the qiyas.

Core Idea
The sale of grain in its spike is permissible because the grain is beneficial property and the hadith implies permission after ripening.

This passage addresses a classic disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the sale of grains and nuts while still in their inedible coverings. The Hanafi school permits such sales, relying on a hadith of the Prophet ﷺ and the principle that the grain is māl mutaqawwim. The Shafi'i school prohibits it by analogy to goldsmith's dust. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate qiyas against explicit textual evidence (nass).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafis permit selling wheat in spike, beans in pod, rice, sesame, and all nuts in shells. The ruling is general: all such sales are permissible.
The text explicitly says 'عندنا يجوز ذلك كله' (according to us, all of that is permissible).
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Imam Shafi'i prohibits selling green beans, walnuts, almonds, etc., in their outer shells, and has two opinions on selling spikes. His basis: the edible part is covered by something useless.
The Shafi'i view is not uniform on spikes, showing some internal flexibility.
3
Examine the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i proof is qiyas: the covering has no benefit, so the transaction resembles selling goldsmith's dust for its own genus, which is prohibited due to ribā risk.
Goldsmith's dust is sold for its gold content; here the covering is not the object of sale.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis cite a hadith: the Prophet forbade selling spikes until they become white and safe from blight. The prohibition before a condition implies permission after. Also, grain is beneficial property (māl mutaqawwim), unlike goldsmith's dust which has no intrinsic benefit.
The hadith is ahad (single transmission) but acceptable for establishing rulings in Hanafi usul.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis can execute such sales validly; Shafi'is cannot (except the spike in one opinion). This affects farmers and traders in Hanafi-majority regions.
The difference is real: a Shafi'i merchant would refuse to buy wheat in the ear.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
گندم اور چاول کی بیع بالیوں میں اور لوبیا اور تل کی بیع چھلکے میں کرنے کا حکم
ويجوز بيع الحنطة فى سنبلها والباقلى فى قشره وكذا الارز والسمسم وقال الشافعي لا يجوز بيع الباقلى الاخضر و كذا الجوز واللوز والفستق في قشره الأول عنده وله فى بيع السنبلة قولان وعندنا يجوز ذالك کله له ان المعقود عليه مستور بما لا منفعة له فيه فاشبه تراب الصاغة اذا بيع بجنسه ولنا ماروى عن النبي عليه السلام انه نهى عن بيع النخل حتى يزهى وعن بيع السنبل حتى يبيض ويا من العاهة ولانه حب منتفع به فيجوز بيعه في سنبله كالشعير والجامع كونه مالا متقوما بخلاف تراب الصاغه لانه انما لايجوز بيعه بجنسه لاحتمال الربا حتى لو باعه بخلاف جنسه جازوفی مسئلتنا لو باعه بجنسه لا يجوز ايضا لشبهة الربوا لانه لایدرى قدر مافى السنابل
ترجمہ اور گندم کا اس کی بالوں میں اور لوہے کا اس کی پھلی میں بیچنا جائز ہے۔ اور یہی حکم چاول اور تل کا ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ سبز لوبیے کی بیع جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہی حکم بادام، پستہ اور اخروٹ کا اس کے موٹے چھلکے میں ہے۔ اور بالیوں میں گندم فروخت کرنے کے بارے میں امام شافعی کے دو قول ہیں اور ہمارے نزدیک یہ سب جائز ہیں۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ معقود علیہ ایسی چیز کے اندر مستور ہے جس میں کوئی نفع نہیں ہے تو زرگروں کی راکھ کے مشابہ ہوگی جبکہ اپنی جنس کے عوض فروخت کی جائے اور
The Ruling on Selling Wheat and Rice in Spikes, and Beans and Sesame in Their Husks
It is permissible to sell wheat in its spike, and beans in their pod, and likewise rice and sesame. Al-Shafi‘i said: It is not permissible to sell green beans, and likewise walnuts, almonds, and pistachios in their outer shell according to him. And regarding selling the spike (of grain), he has two opinions. According to us (Hanafis), all of that is permissible. His (Shafi‘i's) proof is that the contracted object is covered by something that has no benefit, so it resembles goldsmith's dust when sold with its like. Our proof is what was narrated from the Prophet ﷺ that he forbade selling dates until they ripen and spikes until they become white and safe from blight. And because it is a beneficial grain, so it is permissible to sell it in its spike like barley. The common element is that it is valuable property (māl mutaqawwim), unlike goldsmith's dust, because it is not permissible to sell it with its own kind due to the possibility of ribā, even if sold with other than its kind it is permissible. And in our issue, if it is sold with its own kind, it is also not permissible due to the suspicion of ribā because the amount in the spikes is not known.
Translation: And selling wheat in its spike and beans in their pod is permissible. The same ruling applies to rice and sesame. Imam Shafi‘i said: Selling green beans is not permissible, and likewise walnuts, almonds, and pistachios in their outer shell according to him. Regarding selling the spike of wheat, he has two opinions. And according to us (Hanafis), all of that is permissible. The proof of Imam Shafi‘i is that the contracted object is covered by something that has no benefit, so it resembles goldsmith's dust when sold with its own kind. Our proof is what was narrated from the Prophet ﷺ that he forbade selling dates until they turn red and spikes until they become white and safe from blight. And because it is a beneficial grain, so it is permissible to sell it in its spike like barley. The common element is that it is valuable property, unlike goldsmith's dust, because it is not permissible to sell it with its own kind due to the possibility of ribā, even if sold with other than its kind it is permissible. And in our issue, if it is sold with its own kind, it is also not permissible due to the suspicion of ribā because the amount in the spikes is not known.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi‘i schools regarding the sale of grains and nuts while still in their inedible coverings (spikes, pods, shells). The Hanafi position is that such sales are permissible. The text lists examples: wheat in spike, beans in pod, rice, sesame, and by extension walnuts, almonds, pistachios in their shells. The Shafi‘i position is generally impermissible, though Shafi‘i has two opinions on selling spikes. The Shafi‘i proof is qiyās: the edible part is concealed by a useless covering, analogous to goldsmith's dust (turāb al-ṣāghah), which cannot be sold for its own genus due to ribā risk. The Hanafi response (our proof) is based on a hadith: the Prophet ﷺ forbade selling dates until they ripen and spikes until they become white and safe from blight. This implies that after these conditions are met, sale is allowed. Additionally, Hanafis argue that grain is valuable property (māl mutaqawwim), and the covering does not render the sale invalid because the grain is beneficial and the covering is not a distraction. The passage also notes that if the grain in spike is sold with its own kind (e.g., wheat for wheat), it may involve ribā due to unknown quantity, so such sales might be restricted—but the general sale with cash or other items is permissible. The passage type is clearly an inter-madhhab dispute with textual proof (hadith) on the Hanafi side.

Key Terms
سنبل (sunbul): The spike or ear of grain containing the seeds.
قشر (qishr): The outer husk, pod, or shell of a grain or nut.
تراب الصاغة (turāb al-ṣāghah): Dust collected from goldsmiths' workshops that contains gold particles; its sale for like genus is prohibited due to possibility of ribā.
مال متقوم (māl mutaqawwim): Legally recognized property that has material value and is permissible to benefit from.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi proof for allowing the sale of grain in its spike?
A) Qiyas with the sale of wool on a sheep.
B) The hadith that the Prophet forbade selling spikes until they become white, implying permission thereafter.
C) Ijma' of all companions.
D) The principle that everything is permissible unless prohibited.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits sale of grain in its covering based on prophetic hadith and the beneficial nature of grain, rejecting the Shafi'i analogy to goldsmith's dust.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Excluding Known Weight in Fruit Sales: Hanafi Dispute
Dispute within Hanafi school and with other schools on exclusion of known weight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on excluding known weight in fruit sales and evaluate the arguments of the opposing view.

Core Idea
A known weight that can be sold alone can be excepted without invalidating the sale.

This lesson unpacks an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sale of fruits still on trees when the seller excludes a specific known weight (e.g., 10 kg). While some narrations from Abu Hanifa and other schools prohibit such exceptions due to uncertainty, the authoritative Zahir al-Riwayah position validates them if the excepted amount could be sold independently. We will explore the reasoning behind both views and see how the Hanafi masters prioritized the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Zahir al-Riwayah)
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, the sale is valid if the excepted weight is known and can be sold alone. The principle: 'Whatever can be sold alone can be excepted.'
2
Identify the opposing view
Hasan ibn Ziyad's narration from Abu Hanifa, along with Imam Tahawi, Shafi'i, and Ahmad, holds the sale invalid due to gharar (uncertainty of remaining fruits).
3
Follow the opposing proof
The exception renders the remaining fruits unknown in weight, causing excessive uncertainty that invalidates the contract.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The sale is by estimation (kharṣ), not weight; visual observation suffices. If the exception equals the total produce, the exception is void, and the sale covers all fruits.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, the mufta bihi Hanafi position permits such exceptions, while opposing views (even within the school) do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مشائخ نے فرمایا ہے کہ درختوں پر پھلوں کے بیچنے اور ارطال معلومہ کا استثناء کرنے کی صورت میں بیع کا عدم جواز امام ابو حنیفہ سے حسن بن زیاد کی روایت ہے۔ اور یہی امام طحاوی کا قول ہے۔ اور امام شافعی اور امام احمد بھی اسی کے قاتل ہیں۔ اور رہا ظاہر الروایہ کا حکم تو اس کے مطابق ارطال معلومہ کا استثناء کرنے کی صورت میں بھی جائز ہونی چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ ظاہر الروایہ میں یہ ضابطہ ذکر کیا گیا ہے کہ جس چیز کو تنہا فروخت کرنا جائز ہے اس کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز ہے۔ اور جس کو تنہا بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے اس کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً اناج کے ڈھیر میں سے ایک قفیز کی بیع جائز ہے تو پورے ڈھیر کو بیچنا اور ایک قفیز کو مستی کرنا بھی جائز ہے ۔ اور چونکہ فقط حمل کو بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ مثلا یوں کہے کہ میں نے اس بکری کو فروخت کیا نہ کہ اس کے حمل کو اور اسی طرح چونکہ حیوان کے تنہا عضو کو بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے اس لئے اس کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز نہ ہوگا۔ مثلاً یوں کہے کہ میں نے اس بکری کو بیچا لیکن اس کی کھال کو نہیں بیچا۔ پس اس طرح چونکہ باغ کے پھلوں میں سے ارطال معلومہ کا تنہا بیچنا جائز ہے تو ارطال معلومہ کا استثناء کرنا بھی جائز ہوگا۔ اور رہا یہ کہنا کہ مقدار مستثنیٰ کے بعد جو پھیل باقی ہیں وہ مجہول ہیں۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ بلاشبہ مجہول ہیں لیکن وزن کے اعتبار سے مجہول ہیں۔ مشاہدہ کے اعتبار سے مجہول نہیں ہیں۔ اور یہاں پھلوں کی بیع اندازہ سے کی گئی ہے نہ کہ وزن سے اور بیچ جب اندازہ سے کی جاتی ہے تو سبیع کا وزن یا کیل کے اعتبار سے معلوم ہونا ضروری نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اشارہ اور مشاہدہ سے معلوم ہونا کافی ہوتا ہے اور سیہ بات یہاں موجود ہے۔ اسلئے ارطال معلومہ کا استثناء کرنے کے باوجود بیچ درست ہوگی۔ اور رہا یہ کہنا کہ بسا اوقات پھلی اس قدر ہوتے ہیں جس قدر کا استثناء کیا گیا ہے تو مبیع ہی معدوم ہو جائے گی۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں گل کا استثناء گل سے ہوگا۔ اور گل کا استثنا محل سے باطل ہوتا ہے پس جب استثناء باطل ہوگیا تو بلا استثناء تمام پھلوں کی بیچ ہوئی۔ اور بلا استثناء باغ کے تمام پھلوں کی بیع جائز ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے اس صورت میں بھی بیع جائز ہوگی۔
The author of Hidayah states that the Mashayikh said: The impermissibility of selling fruits on trees while excluding known pounds is a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyād from Imam Abu Hanifa. This is also the view of Imam Tahawi. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad also hold this view. As for the ruling of Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, according to it, excluding known pounds should be permissible. Because in Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah it is stated as a principle: Whatever can be sold alone, its exception is also permissible; and whatever cannot be sold alone, its exception is also not permissible. For example, selling one qafiz from a heap of grain is permissible, so selling the entire heap while excepting one qafiz is also permissible. And since selling the fetus alone is not permissible, its exception is also not permissible—e.g., saying 'I sold this goat but not its fetus.' Similarly, since selling a single limb of an animal alone is not permissible, its exception is not permissible—e.g., 'I sold this goat but not its skin.' Thus, since selling known pounds of the garden's fruits alone is permissible, the exception of known pounds is also permissible. As for the objection that the remaining fruits after the exception are unknown, we say: They are indeed unknown in terms of weight, but not unknown in terms of observation. Here the sale of fruits is based on estimation, not on weight. When a sale is by estimation, it is not necessary that the weight or measure of the sold item be known; rather, it is sufficient that it be known by indication and observation, and this is present here. Therefore, the sale is valid despite the exception of known pounds. As for the objection that sometimes the fruits are exactly equal to the amount excepted, so the sold item would be non-existent, the answer is that in that case the exception of part from the whole would be made, and the exception of part from the whole is void. So when the exception is void, the entire fruits are sold without exception, and selling all the garden fruits without exception is permissible. Hence, the sale is valid in this case as well.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of selling fruits on trees while excluding a known weight (e.g., 10 kg). According to a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyād from Imam Abu Hanifa, such an exception renders the sale invalid. This view is also held by Imam Tahawi, Imam Shafi'i, and Imam Ahmad. However, the relied-upon position in the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah (the core transmitted works) holds that it is valid, based on a general principle: anything that can be sold alone can be excepted. Since selling a known weight of fruit alone is permissible (e.g., if they are already picked), excepting them from a sale is also permissible. The commentary then refutes objections: (1) The remaining fruits are unknown in weight, but that is acceptable because the sale is based on estimation and visual inspection, not precise weight. (2) If the exception equals the entire produce, the exception is void, and the sale of all fruits stands valid. This demonstrates the Hanafi method of legal reasoning, using principles (uṣūl) to resolve apparent contradictions.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithnāʾ): The act of excluding a specific part of the sold item from the sale contract.
ارطال معلومة (arṭāl maʿlūmah): A known number of pounds (a specific weight) that the seller excludes from the fruit sale.
ظاہر الروایہ (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that contain the authoritative Hanafi rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, if a person sells all the fruits in his garden but excludes 10 kg, what is the ruling?
A) The sale is invalid because the remaining fruits are unknown in weight.
B) The sale is valid because selling 10 kg alone is permissible, and the exception follows that rule.
C) The sale is invalid unless the buyer agrees to the exception.
D) The sale becomes a separate contract for the excepted fruits.

Key Takeaway
A known weight that can be sold independently may be excepted from a sale of fruits on trees without invalidating the contract, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.
